## 1. Objectives of the program

The objectives of the ECE program are to train the students the knowledge and the skills on electrical and computer engineering in the research activities and industrial application. That is reflected in the following competencies of the graduates:

- The graduates  become practicing engineers in fields such as design, research, development, testing, manufacturing, operations and service systems. They may pursue a diverse range of positions such as engineers, consultants, planning officers, entrepreneurs in public, private institutions and start-up companies.
- Engineering  ethos :  the  graduates  have  the  laboratory  skills  and  the  ability  to  use modern  analysis,  design  techniques  and  state-of-the-art  equipment  to  solve  practical engineering problems. Through project-oriented tasks in dealing with practical and jobrelated examples, graduates apply their knowledge, recognize their knowledge gaps and are able to close them according to specific requirements.
- Professional skills and leadership : the graduates have the professional skills to function effectively  in  the  work  environment  as  well  as  in  the  community.  The  impact  of  ECE graduates  is  measured  not  only  by  their  individual  technical  innovations,  but  also  by their influence on their teams and companies, and in their fields Graduates are prepared to conduct effective project and/or executive management.
- Engagement :  the  graduates  have  a  solid  understanding  of  professional  and  ethical responsibility, committed to ethical action and engaged in life-long learning to remain effective  members  of  their  communities  and  thoughtful  contributors  to  society, economy and ecology.
- Versatility :  the  graduates  apply  their  abilities,  talents,  and  insights  creatively  and productively  in  fields  and  professions  the  curriculum.  They  acquire  social  skills  and engineering  expertise  according  to  German  standards  in  order  to  adapt  and  work effectively in the multi-disciplinary, Vietnamese and international work environments.
- Constant development : the graduates have the ability to engage in life-long learning and recognize  that  the  practice  of  electrical  engineering  is  constantly  evolving  and  that engineers must have the ability to acquire new knowledge and skills on their own.

## 2. Intended learning outcomes of the program

The  ECE  program  at  VGU  is  committed  to  impart  the  following learning  outcomes .  The graduates will be able to:

| No.   | Intended learning outcomes                                                                                                                                                              |
|-------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| ILO1  | Apply appropriate mathematical, science and core engineering methods to identify, formulate and solve electrical and computer engineering related problems;                             |
| ILO2  | Use conventional software and hardware tools and equipment to design and conduct experiments, test and evaluate analogue and digital systems, as well as to analyze and interpret data; |
| ILO3  | Analyze, design, program, develop and evaluate complex electrical, electronic systems, automation systems, embedded systems, power systems,                                             |

| No.   | Intended learning outcomes                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
|-------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|       | communication systems to meet desired requirements in terms of general quality attributes and possible trade-offs presented within the given problem;                                                                                                                                                    |
| ILO4  | Retrieve and analyze information from different sources, including information retrieval through databases and online computer searches;                                                                                                                                                                 |
| ILO5  | Demonstrate competency in English and Vietnamese oral and written communication skills, as well as in the use of relevant computing technologies and modern engineering tools necessary for engineering practice;                                                                                        |
| ILO6  | Develop deeper understanding of a certain disciplinary area in electrical and computer engineering;                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| ILO7  | Prepare high quality engineering documents and present a clear and coherent presentation of these to a range of technical and nontechnical audiences;                                                                                                                                                    |
| ILO8  | Function professionally in a globally competitive world, and to work as members of a team;                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| ILO9  | Work collaboratively in multi-disciplinary teams to plan and execute project work or research in the electrical, electronics and computer engineering disciplines.                                                                                                                                       |
| ILO10 | Understand ethical principles and their role in the engineering profession; committed to ethical action and engaged in life-long learning to remain effective members of their communities; have the skills and attitudes to be responsible and thoughtful contributors to society, economy and ecology. |

## Prerequisites

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

-  Get familiar with majors and perspectives in ECE program
-  Improve hand-on skills to built a work project
-  Independently study and search documents related to the topics
-  Practice team working and enhance reporting/presentation skill

: Consists of Lectures and Labs

| No.                             | Topic                                                                              |

| 2.                              | Seminar regarding research and technology in one of the branches                   |
| 3.                              | Seminar regarding research and technology in one of the branches                   |
| 4.                              | Seminar regarding research and technology in one of the branches                   |
| 5.                              | Seminar regarding research and technology in one of the branches                   |
| 6.                              | Seminar regarding research and technology in one of the branches                   |

| Lab session - SoccerBot contest | Lab session - SoccerBot contest                                                    |

| 9.                              | Assemble SoccerBot using Solid Edge ST9                                            |
| 10.                             | 3D Printing                                                                        |
| 11.                             | Printed Circuit Board production procedure                                         |
| 12.                             | Arduino communication via Bluetooth or Wifi                                        |
| 13.                             | Test the components and working principles of the robot                            |
| 14.                             | Testing the whole system/robot and troubleshoot issues                             |
| 15.                             | Final contest                                                                      |

Module title

English for Engineering

Module code

61ECE102

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer

| Type               | Lecturer        | Email                 | Office   | Office hours (if any)              |
|--------------------|-----------------|-----------------------|----------|------------------------------------|

Semester

Winter Semester

## Student workload

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency Once each academic year

## Prerequisites

## No prerequisite is needed.

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Understand the basics of patent laws in Vietnam, Europe, the UK and the US.
2. Demonstrate capacity to draft a patent application.
3. Understand the basics on how to research for and find available grants as well as how to begin the grant process.
4. Demonstrate capacity to prepare a competitive grant proposals based on a finished prototype, published patent applications and/or research papers.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
|-------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Invention as a solution to an unsolved problem  Priority of patents: concepts of 'first to file'.  Paris convention/PCT.  Patentability criteria (novelty, inventive step, industrial applicability)  Non-patentable subject matters, including plant/animals varieties, method for prevention, diagnosis or treatment of diseases, animals or plants, topographical design of integrated circuits and computer programs.  Utility Innovations  Difference between the different patenting systems, including Vietnam, UK, US, EP and WPO. |
|    2. | Drafting a patent  Structure of the patent specification  Types and arrangement of claims  Drafting a claim                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
|    3. | Filing a priority patent application                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
|    4. | Amending the patent description and filing a new application on the top of the priority application.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
|    5. | Prosecuting a patent application  Patent search and examination                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
|    6. | Funding sources and finding best practices.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
|    7. | Pros and Cons of Community Partnerships  Understanding the advantages and disadvantages of including community partners in the pre-writing planning process, the writing process, the implementation process, and the evaluation process.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
|    8. | Writing a grant proposal based on a finished prototype, published patent applications and/or research papers.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |

-  Describing the project team, organization.
-  Developing a Compelling Problem Statement.
-  Describing the Request to the Funder.
-  Writing a Program Design and Planning the Evaluation Process.
-  Demonstrating Sustainability.
-  Planning the Budget
-  Recommended Attachments: Photos, Measured Results, published patents, research papers.

## Learning activities

| Activities             | Explanation                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
|------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Attendance             | Students should attend 100%. Attendance will be checked every lesson. There is no grade for the attendance completion.                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| Individual Assignments | A classroom assignment will be given right after each lecture to enhance the students' learning and development.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| Online Activities      | A forum will be created on VGU's e-learning platform for student discussion and share on topics and individual works.                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| Self-study             | Online learning materials together with a handful of recommended video lectures will be given during the course                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| Lab or Workshop        | Students will be given a lab session to 1) Conduct a patent search based on a case study; 2) Draft a patent application, including a complete patent specifications and claim; 3) File a priority application; 4) File an amended patent application; 5) Write a proposal. 6) Present the proposed ideas. 7) To peer review other students' work. |

## Mode of Assessment

Assignments:

Classroom assignments will be given right after each sub-module. (10 marks)

## Lab sessions:

The lab assignments will be graded according to

1. the novelties as revealed by peer reviews and their patent searches (15 marks);
2. the results of formality checks (10 marks);
3. the conciseness of the patent specification (20 marks);
4. the quality of the proposal according to the peer reviews (20 marks);
5. the  quality  of  the  student's  peer  review  report  according  to  the  course  instructor's judgment (15 marks).

## Exams

- Oral presentation: 15 minutes (10 marks)

## Grading policy

| Assessment method   |   Percentage of total | Assessment date          |
|---------------------|-----------------------|--------------------------|
| Oral examination    |                    10 | At the end of the course |
| Class Assignments   |                    10 | Frequently               |
| Lab Assignments     |                    80 | At the end of the course |
| Total               |                   100 |                          |

## Required software

1. Latex
2. Octave
3. R
4. WebPlotDigitizer

|---------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Self-study          | Where necessary, students need to learn or revise grammar and vocabulary that they are unfamiliar with or weak at. |

## Mode of Assessment

Mini tests: Students are given one full listening, reading &amp; writing practice test in class midway through the module, and a review of the these tests is also conducted as feedback.

## Exams

As per standard for an official IELTS test, i.e. no materials are allowed to  be used during the test. The exceptions are the student's own pencil, pen and eraser. One full three-hour IELTS test is given at the end of the module.

Module title

German 1

Module code

61ECE107

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer

| Type                                                 | Lecturer          | Email             | Office   | Office hours (if any)          |
|------------------------------------------------------|-------------------|-------------------|----------|--------------------------------|
| Module Coordinator                                   | MA. Tran Tuan Anh | anh.tt@vgu.edu.vn | A.206    | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon to Fri      |
| Lecturer German Teachers of the German Language Unit | None              |                   | A.206    | 9:00 AM - 16:00 PM, Mon to Fri |

Classification

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

## Semester Winter Semester

## Student workload

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency The module is offered each year

Prerequisites

IELTS 6.0

Applicability for other modules Completing this module is a prerequisite for module of German 2

Intended learning outcomes (based on the description for basic user of language of CEFR beginner level)

After this course, learners of German language can:

1. Comprehend and use familiar everyday expressions and very basic phrases aiming at meeting the needs of a concrete type.
2. Introduce oneself and others; ask for and give information about personal details such as address, friends and belongings.
3. Interact in a simple way if the interlocutor talks slowly and clearly and is ready to help.

Contents In this first German course for beginners, students shall study the first six lessons from the course book Studio 21 A1 which offers different topics related to very simple daily communication situations

|   No. | Topic                              |
|-------|------------------------------------|
|    1. | Introduction: Start auf Deutsch    |
|    2. | Unit 1: Kaffee oder Tee?           |
|    3. | Unit 2: Sprache im Kurs            |
|    4. | Unit 3: Städte - Länder - Sprachen |
|    5. | Review of units 1-3: Station 1     |
|    6. | Unit 4: Menschen und Häuser        |
|    7. | Unit 5: Termine                    |
|    8. | Unit 6: Orientierung               |
|    9. | Review of units 4-6: Station 2     |

## Learning activities

The  teaching  methods  of  the  courses  of  the  German  language  should  mainly  base  on  the following principles

-  Intercultural communicative method: By studying with German course books, Students are encouraged to learn cultures, including their own, and use this understanding (thereof) to communicate with people successfully.
-  Learner-centered teaching method: Students are the focus of all class activities in class, not the instructors.
-  Learning by doing: class activities are organized in various social forms such as interviews, teamwork, games, mini-projects, discussions, presentations, etc. Students should use the learning language to fulfill the given tasks.
-  Content integrated language learning (CLIL): The course does not concentrate on the knowledge of German grammar, but on the skills of using the German language. The contents of the language tasks are more important than the language formality.

| Activities   | Explanation                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
|--------------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Attendance   | Students must attend at least 80% of sessions during the course. Attendance will be checked in every session. Students being absent more than 20% of the sessions will not be allowed to take the final exam. |
| Self-study   | Students should do all the self-study tasks being offered in the course books and do all the homework given by the lecturer                                                                                   |

## Mode of Assessment

Mini test: 1 mid-term test will be given as an in-class test after the half of course duration. The test comprises  4 parts of the language skills (listening  comprehension,  reading comprehension,  vocabulary  &amp;  grammar,  and  writing).  It  consists  of  50  -  60  points  in total and takes around 45 - 60 minutes

## Final exam: The final exam includes 4 separate parts of language skills

1. Listening comprehension: duration: 15 minutes | number of points: 10

2. Reading comprehension: duration: 20 minutes | number of points: 10

3. Vocabulary &amp; Grammar: duration: 30 minutes | number of points: 30

4.

Writing: duration: 20 minutes | number of points: 10

## Grading policy

| Assessment method   |   Percentage of total | Assessment date                                                        |
|---------------------|-----------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Midterm test        |                    30 | After the half of course duration (in the 13 th session of the course) |
| Final exam          |                    70 | At the end of the course (after 8 weeks)                               |
| Total               |                   100 |                                                                        |

Intended learning  outcomes (based  on  the  description  for  basic  user  of  language  of  CEFR  beginner level)

After this course, learners of German language can:

1. Comprehend and use familiar everyday expressions and very basic phrases aiming at meeting the needs of a concrete type.
2. Introduce oneself and others; ask for and give information about personal details such as address, friends and belongings.
3. Interact in a simple way if the interlocutor talks slowly and clearly and is ready to help.

Module title

Calculus

Module code

61ECE111

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer

| Type                    | Lecturer             | Email               | Office   | Office hours (if any)   | Office hours (if any)   |
|-------------------------|----------------------|---------------------|----------|-------------------------|-------------------------|
| Module Coordinator      | Dr. Phạm Thành Dương | duong.pt@vgu.edu.vn | B110     | 8:00-16:30, to Fri      | Mon                     |
| Lecturer                | Dr. Phạm Thành Dương | duong.pt@vgu.edu.vn | B110     | 8:00-16:30, to Fri      | Mon                     |
| Tutorial Dr. Phạm Dương | Thành                | duong.pt@vgu.edu.vn | B110     | 8:00-16:30, to Fri      | Mon                     |

Classification

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

Semester

Summer Semester

## Student workload

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites

None

Applicability  for  other  modules This  course  is  a  prerequisite  for  the  course  Advanced Engineering Mathematics

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. To provide the students with the main ideas and techniques of calculus, concerning limits, continuity, differentiation and integration, ordinary differential equations.
2. To provide an understanding of the practical meaning, significance and applications of these ideas and techniques, through practical examples taken from many areas of engineering, business and the life sciences
3. To develop skills in mathematical modelling and problem solving, in thinking logically, and in creatively applying existing knowledge to new situations
4. To develop confidence and fluency in discussing mathematics in English.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
|-------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Functions, Limits and Continuity 1. What is Calculus? 2. Straight Lines. Equations of Lines 3. Functions and Graphs 4. New Functions from Old Functions. Inverse Functions 5. Parametric Curves 6. Definition of a Limit. One-sided Limits 7. Laws of Limits. Evaluating Limits. The Squeeze Theorem 1.8 Continuity 1.9 The Intermediate Value Theorem 1.10 Limits Involving Infinity |
|    2. | Differentiation 2.1 The Tangent and Velocity Problems. Rates of Change 2.2 The Derivative. Higher-Order Derivatives 3. Rules of Differentiation. Finding Derivatives using Mathematica (Matlab)                                                                                                                                                                                       |



4. Rates of Change in the Natural and Social Sciences
5. Implicit Differentiation
6. Differentiation of Inverse Functions
7. Linear Approximations. Differentials

## Applications of Differentiation

1. Related Rates
2. Maxima and Minima. Critical Points
3. The Mean Value Theorem. The First Derivative Test. Concavity. Shapes of Curves.
4. Curve Sketching.  Graphing with Calculus and Computers using Maple
5. Indeterminate Forms and l'Hôpital's Rules
6. Maxima and Minima Problems
7. Newton's Method
8. Anti-derivatives and Indefinite Integrals

## Integration

1. Areas under Curves and Distances
2. The Definite Integral
3. Properties of the Definite Integral.
4. The Fundamental Theorem of Calculus
5. Integration by  Substitution
6. 4.6 Integration by Parts
4. 4.7 Additional Techniques of Integration. Partial Fractions
8. 4.8 Integration Using Tables and Computer Algebra Systems
9. 4.9 Numerical Integration
10. 4.10 Improper Integrals

## Applications of Integration

- 5.1 Areas between Curves
- 5.2 Areas Enclosed by Parametric Curves
- 5.3 Volumes
5. 5.4 Arc Length
- 5.5 Average Value of a Function
- 5.6 Applications to Engineering, Economics and     Science

## Ordinary differential equations

- 6.1 Differential equations
6. 6.2 Separable equations
- 6.3 First order linear differential equations
- 6.4 Second order differential equations

## Learning activities

| Activities             | Explanation                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
|------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Attendance             | Students should attend 100%. Attendance will be checked regularly. There is no grade for the attendance completion.                                                                                                                                               |
| Individual Assignments | Regular assignments are given to test students' learning and development.                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| Group work             | Each 5-member group will develop a project                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| Online Activities      | A forum will be created on VGU's e-learning platform for student discussion and share on topics, group and individual works. Students are required to post the group project report on the site. All students are required to read all group reports and comment. |
| Self-study             | Students are expected to spend time on preparing for the lectures and tutorials                                                                                                                                                                                   |

## Mode of Assessment

Assignments:

2 or 3 assignments.

Midterm examination:

Midterm test will be organized in the middle of the course.

- Length of examination: 60 minutes
- Basic calculators and 2 sheets of A4 paper with notes are allowed in the exam room.

## Final examination:

- Length of examination: 90 minutes
- Basic calculators and 2 sheets of A4 paper with notes are allowed in the exam room.

## Grading policy

| Assessment method   |   Percentage of total | Assessment date                   |
|---------------------|-----------------------|-----------------------------------|
| Assignments         |                    20 |                                   |
| Midterm examination |                    20 | The 9 th week of the course       |
| Final examination   |                    60 | One or two weeks after the course |
| Total               |                   100 |                                   |

61ECE112

Frequency

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites

None

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. To  provide  the  students  with  the  main  ideas  and  techniques  of  linear  algebra, concerning complex numbers, permutations, matrices, determinant, linear transformation and systems of linear equations.
2. To provide an understanding of the practical meaning, significance and applications of these ideas and techniques, through practical examples taken from many areas of engineering, business and the life sciences
3. To develop skills in mathematical modelling and problem solving, in thinking logically, and in creatively applying existing knowledge to new situations
4. To develop confidence and fluency in discussing mathematics in English.

## Contents

| No.   | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
|-------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 1.    | Complex Numbers 1. What is a complex number? 2. Basic Operations 3. Geometric Interpretation 4. Polar form                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| 2.    | Matrices 2.1 Permutations 2.2 Matrices and basic properties 3. Basic definitions: transpose matrices, zero matrices, identity matrices, triangular matrices, symmetric and skew-symmetric matrices. 4. Basic operations: addition, subtraction, scalar and matrix multiplications 5. Invertible matrices 6. Differentiation of Inverse Functions 7. Linear Approximations. Differentials |
|      | Determinants 1. Definition of determinants 2. Basic properties 3. Laplace's formula 4. Triangularization of matrices 5. Ranks of matrices 6. Inverse of matrices                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| 4.    | Systems of linear equations 1. Systems of linear equations 2. Solvability 3. Solving methods: Cramer's rule, Gaussian elimination                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| 5.    | Vector spaces 5.1 Definition of vector spaces 5.2 Linear Independence 5.3 Bases and dimensions 5.4 Linear subspaces 5.5 Solution spaces of homogeneous systems of linear equations                                                                                                                                                                                                       |

## 5.6 Applications to Engineering, Economics and Science

Semester

Summer Semester

## Student workload

| Credits                              |   6 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency

The module is offered each academic year

## Prerequisites

Proficiency in high school physics, and mathematics

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

-  Demonstrate converting units and other aspects of dimensional analysis in the working of numerical problems.
-  Apply principles of Newtonian mechanics to predict and account for simple phenomena modeled by the motion of particles in one and two dimensions.
-  Apply principles of Newtonian mechanics to predict and account for simple phenomena modeled by the motion of a rigid body in two dimensions.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
|-------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Units, physical quantities, and vectors  Three fundamental quantities of physics and the units physicists use to measure them.  How to keep track of significant figures in your calculations.  The difference between scalars and vectors, and how to add and subtract vectors graphically.  What the components of a vector are, and how to use them in calculations.  What unit vectors are, and how to use them with components to describe vectors.  Two ways of multiplying vectors.                                                                                               |
|    2. | Motion along a straight line  How to describe straight-line motion in terms of average velocity, instantaneous velocity, average acceleration, and instantaneous acceleration.  How to interpret graphs of position versus time, velocity versus time, and acceleration versus time for straight line motion.  How to solve problems involving straight-line motion with constant acceleration, including free-fall problems.  How to analyze straight-line motion when the acceleration is not constant.                                                                                  |
|    3. | Motion in two and three dimensions  How to represent the position of a body in two or three dimensions using vectors.  How to determine the vector velocity of a body from a knowledge of its path.  How to find the vector acceleration of a body, and why a body can have an acceleration even if its speed is constant.  How to interpret the components of a body's acceleration parallel to and perpendicular to its path.  How to describe the curved path followed by a projectile.  The key ideas behind motion in a circular path, with either constant speed or varying speed. |

|    |  How to relate the velocity of a moving body as seen from two different frames of reference.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
|----|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 4. | Newton's laws of motion  What the concept of force means in physics, and why forces are vectors.  The significance of the net force on an object, and what happens when the net force is zero.  The relationship among the net force on an object, the object's mass, and its acceleration.  How the forces that two bodies exert on each other are related.                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| 5. | Applying Newton's laws  How to use Newton's first law to solve problems involving the forces that act on a body in equilibrium.  How to use Newton's second law to solve problems involving the forces that act on an accelerating body.  The nature of the different types of friction forces-static friction, kinetic friction, rolling friction, and fluid resistance-and how to solve problems that involve these forces.  How to solve problems involving the forces that act on a body moving along a circular path.  The key properties of the four fundamental forces of nature. |
| 6. | Work and kinetic energy  What it means for a force to do work on a body, and how to calculate the amount of work done.  The definition of the kinetic energy (energy of motion) of a body, and what it means physically.  How the total work done on a body changes the body's kinetic energy, and how to use this principle to solve problems in mechanics.  How to use the relationship between total work and change in kinetic energy when the forces are not constant, the body follows a curved path, or both.  How to solve problems involving power (the rate of doing work).    |
| 7. | Potential energy and energy conservation                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |

9.

-  How to use the concept of gravitational potential energy in problems that involve vertical motion.
-  How to use the concept of elastic potential energy in problems that involve a moving body attached to a stretched or compressed spring.
-  The distinction between conservative and non-conservative forces, and how to solve problems in which both kinds of forces act on a moving body.
-  How to calculate the properties of a conservative force if you know the corresponding potential-energy function.
-  How to use energy diagrams to understand the motion of an object moving in a straight line under the influence of a conservative force. it means for a force to do work on a body, and how to calculate the amount of work done.

## Momentum, impulse, and collisions

-  The meaning of the momentum of a particle, and how the impulse of the net force acting on a particle causes its momentum to change.
-  The conditions under which the total momentum of a system of particles is constant (conserved).
-  How to solve problems in which two bodies collide with each other.
8.  The important distinction among elastic, inelastic, and completely inelastic collisions.
-  The definition of the center of mass of a system, and what determines how the center of mass moves.
-  How to analyze situations such as rocket propulsion in which the mass of a body changes as it moves.

## Rotation of rigid bodies

-  How to describe the rotation of a rigid body in terms of angular coordinate, angular velocity, and angular acceleration.
-  How  to  analyze  rigid-body  rotation  when  the  angular  acceleration  is constant.
-  How to relate the rotation of a rigid body to the linear velocity and linear acceleration of a point on the body.
-  The meaning of a body's moment of inertia about a rotation axis, and how

it relates to rotational kinetic energy.

-  How to calculate the moment of inertia of various bodies.

|------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

| Individual Assignments | Bi-weekly assignments                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| Lab or Workshop        | Experiment 2- Determine the moment of inertia of rigid sphere, a dish, a cylinder, a long bar. Experiment 3 - Determine the wavelength of a laser beam Interference at Fresnel's Bi-prism and mirror with an He-Ne each experiment students have to collect and analyze |

- No materials, reference are allowed in the exam room.

Module title

Engineering Design

Module code

61ECE114

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Student workload

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |

Frequency The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites

None

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the student will be able to:

1. understand the creative process of innovative product design;
2. balance competing technical, commercial, socio-environmental concerns in engineering design;
3. apply a methodical approach to the solution of engineering design problems;
4. to identify the customer needs to be satisfied by an engineering design;
5. gather design information based on the knowledge of a wide spectrum of information sources;
6. generate conceptual solutions that are broad in how they accomplish their functions but are also feasible;
7. make decisions to select options from a set of alternatives;
8. take  a  design  concept  to  an  embodiment  design  focusing  on  function,  form,  fit,  and finish;
9. appreciate the tasks to be performed during the detailed design phase;
10. use  computational  tools  to  aid  the  application  of  theoretical  models  to  the quantitative design of functional components;
11. communicate in a professional and scientific manner;
12. work effectively and efficiently in a design team.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                                    |
|-------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | The engineering design process                                           |
|    2. | The product development process and product cycles                       |
|    3. | Problem definition and requirement analysis                              |
|    4. | Laboratory 1: 3D solid modeling and 2D engineering drawing: Assignment 1 |
|    5. | Design teams and tools                                                   |
|    6. | Locating information and research                                        |
|    7. | Laboratory 2: Electrical designs: Assignment 2                           |
|    8. | Conceptual design                                                        |
|    9. | Decision making and evaluation processes                                 |
|   10. | Laboratory 3: Electronic circuit simulation: Assignment 3                |
|   11. | Embodiment design                                                        |
|   12. | Detailed design                                                          |
|   13. | Laboratory 4: Electronic design automation (EDA): Assignment 4           |
|   14. | Design for sustainability and the environment                            |
|   15. | Analysis and optimization in design                                      |

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. [Master the most  important concepts and  elements of high-level  programming languages, in particular C and Python in this module, e.g., numbers, strings, assignments, control structures, functions, references and pointers, classes and objects.]

3. [Design simple algorithms and formulate them into a programming code.]
4. [Choose suitable software solutions to develop and program subject-related programming tasks.]
5. [Acquire competences in analytical thinking and structured approach to solving a given problem.]

Module title

Electric Circuits

Module code

61ECE116

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Student workload

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |

Frequency The module is offered each academic year

## Prerequisites

Proficiency  in  high  school  calculus  and  familiarity  with  complex  numbers.  Knowledge  of introductory physics, including electrical and magnetic phenomena.

## Applicability for other modules

## 61ECE313 Electronic Circuits

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the student will be able to:

1. apply the electric circuit problem-solving process to analyze an electric circuit;
2. analyze dc voltages, dc currents, and dc power in linear dc circuits;
3. understand  the  different  methods  to  analyze  electric  circuits,  their  scope,  and  their advantages and disadvantages: parallel components, series components, Δ-to-Y equivalent  circuit,  source  transformation,  Norton  and  Thévenin  equivalent  circuits, node-voltage method, mesh-current method, etc.;
4. select the most appropriate analysis methods for a practical application;
5. perform an electric circuit analysis to find the unknown circuit parameter;
6. determine the power budget in an electric circuit;
7. solve first- and second-order differential equations with constant inputs;
8. understand phasor representation of sinusoidal signals and use the method for solving linear differential equations with sinusoidal inputs;
9. apply the phasor concept to solve circuits for the sinusoidal steady-state response;
10. use active and reactive power in ac circuits, understand the distinction between instantaneous and average power and use the concept of maximum power transfer;
11. analyze various configurations of three-phase ac circuits.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                               |
|-------|---------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | The electric circuit variables: voltage, current, power, and energy |
|    2. | Linear circuit elements: resistors and sources                      |
|    3. | Simple linear circuits                                              |

|   4. | Circuit analysis using the node-voltage and the mesh-current method   |
|------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------|
|   5. | Source transformation and equivalent sources                          |
|   6. | Other circuit analysis methods                                        |
|   7. | Simple nonlinear elements and circuits                                |
|   8. | Introduction to operational amplifiers                                |
|   9. | Operational amplifiers circuits                                       |
|  10. | Alternating voltage and current                                       |
|  11. | Capacitance and inductance                                            |
|  12. | Linear circuit analysis in the phasor domain                          |
|  13. | Transformers                                                          |
|  14. | Power in ac circuits                                                  |
|  15. | Three-phase electric circuits                                         |

In addition to the electric circuit theory, practical examples of techniques and methods to analyze electric circuits are presented in class. Exercises are given to students to be solved in class and open questions regarding the solutions of exercises done at home are discussed in class. |
| Individual Assignments | Exercises are given to students to be solved at home. Open questions regarding the solutions of exercises are discussed in class.                                                                                                                                                                                                               |

Module title

Physics 2

## Student workload

|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|

Frequency

The module is offered each academic year

## Prerequisites

Proficiency in high school physics, and mathematics

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Students  will  be  able  to  conduct  qualitative  analysis  of  electromagnetism  problems which demonstrates conceptual understanding as measured by performance in visualizing  problems  through  diagrams,  estimating  answers,  assessing  and  justifying answers, analyzing graphs and clear, written explanations..
2. Students will be able to perform quantitative calculations in situations involving electric and  magnetic  fields,  and  demonstrate  knowledge  of  the  relevant  basic  units,  vector addition, and application of basic calculus.  Students  will  be  able  to  assess  answers  to questions for plausibility.
3. Students will be able to use simple laboratory demonstrations and computer simulations to explain the basic properties of electric and magnetic fields, and electrical circuits.

## Contents

| No.   | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
|-------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 1.    | Electric charge and electric field The nature of electric charge, and how we know that electric charge is conserved. How objects become electrically charged. How to use Coulomb's law to calculate the electric force between charges. The distinction between electric force and electric field. How to calculate the electric field due to a collection of charges. How to use the idea of electric field lines to visualize and interpret electric fields. How to calculate the properties of electric dipoles. |
| 2.    | Gauss's law  How you can determine the amount of charge within a closed surface by examining the electric field on the surface.  What is meant by electric flux, and how to calculate it.  How Gauss's law relates the electric flux through a closed surface to the charge enclosed by the surface.  How to use Gauss's law to calculate the electric field due to a symmetric charge distribution.  Where the charge is located on a charged conductor.                                                      |
|       | Electric potential                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |

3.

4.

6.

7.

-  How to calculate the electric potential energy of a collection of charges.
-  The meaning and significance of electric potential.
-  How to calculate the electric potential that a collection of charges produces at a point in space.
-  How to use equipotential surfaces to visualize how the electric potential varies in space.
-  How to use electric potential to calculate the electric field

## Capacitance and dielectrics

-  The nature of capacitors, and how to calculate a quantity that measures their ability to store charge.
-  How to analyze capacitors connected in a network.
-  How to calculate the amount of energy stored in a capacitor.
-  What dielectrics are, and how they make capacitors more effective.

## Current, resistance, and electromotive force

-  The meaning of electric current, and how charges move in a conductor.
-  What is meant by the resistivity and conductivity of a substance.
5.  How to calculate the resistance of a conductor from its dimensions and its resistivity.
-  How an electromotive force (emf) makes it possible for current to flow in a circuit. How to do calculations involving energy and power in circuits.

## Direct current circuits

-  How to analyze circuits with multiple resistors in series or parallel.
-  Rules that you can apply to any circuit with more than one loop.
-  How to use an ammeter, voltmeter, ohmmeter, or potentiometer in a circuit.
-  How to analyze circuits that include both a resistor and a capacitor.
-  How electric power is distributed in the home.

## Magnetic field and magnetic force

-  The properties of magnets, and how magnets interact with each other.
-  The nature of the force that a moving charged particle experiences in a magnetic field.
-  How magnetic field lines are different from electric field lines.

8.

9.

-  How to analyze the motion of a charged particle in a magnetic field.
-  Some practical applications of magnetic fields in chemistry and physics.
-  How to analyze magnetic forces on current-carrying conductors.
-  How current loops behave

## Sources of magnetic field

-  The nature of the magnetic field produced by a single moving charged particle.
-  How to describe the magnetic field produced by an element of a currentcarrying conductor.
-  How to calculate the magnetic field produced by a long, straight, currentcarrying wire.
-  Why wires carrying current in the same direction attract, while wires carrying opposing currents repel.
-  How to calculate the magnetic field produced by a current-carrying wire bent into a circle.
-  What Ampere's law is, and what it tells us about magnetic fields.
-  How to use Ampere's law to calculate the magnetic field of symmetric current distributions.

## Electromagnetic induction

-  The experimental evidence that a changing magnetic field induces an emf.
-  How Faraday's law relates the induced emf in a loop to the change in magnetic flux through the loop.
-  How to determine the direction of an induced emf.
-  How to calculate the emf induced in a conductor moving through a magnetic field.
-  How a changing magnetic flux generates an electric field that is very different from that produced by an arrangement of charges.
-  The four fundamental equations that completely describe both electricity and magnetism.

| Activities   | Explanation                                                     |
|--------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------|
| Attendance   | Students should attend around 70%. Attendance will be checked 3 |

|                        | times randomly by submission of 3 mini tests given random tests                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
|------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Individual Assignments | Bi-weekly assignments                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| Lab or Workshop        | Yes Experiment 1- Investigate longitudinal waves, superposition of waves, a reflection of the longitudinal wave; Determine the wavelength of the ultrasonic wave. Experiment 2 - Using Pohn's pendulum to determine Angular frequency, the resonance frequency of torsion pendulum. Experiment 3- Investigate the magnetic field of two Helmholtz coils in the same direction field; in the opposing direction field. After each experiment students have to collect and analyze data then synthesize them on a report. |

Module title:

Electrical Measurement and Instrumentation

Module code:

61ECE202

Study program:

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type               | Lecturer                | Email   | Office                     | Office hours (if any)   |
|--------------------|-------------------------|---------|----------------------------|-------------------------|
| Dr. Bui Minh Duong | duong.bm@vgu.edu.vn     | B111    | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon and Fri | Lecture                 |
| Mr. Nguyen Thinh   | Duc thinh.nd@vgu.edu.vn | B102    | None                       | Lab                     |

Classification:

- [x] ☒ [Compulsory]

- [ ] ☐ [Compulsory optional]

- [ ] ☐ [Optional/Elective]

Semester:

Winter Semester

Student workload:

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites:

None

Applicability for other modules: Fundamental of Power Engineering; Digital Signal Processing; and other modules related to a major of Energy Technology (ET)

Duration:

15 weeks

## Course objective:

This  course  is  to  provide  basic  knowledge  for  ECE  students  about  i)  how  to  present  a measurement problem and solve it by using introductory knowledge of electrical measurement techniques; and ii) how to study on electrical measurements e.g., essential principles of basic circuit analysis, digital logic circuits, transducers and electronic instruments for measurement of physical quantities.

## Intended learning outcomes:

On successful completion of this module, the learner will be able to:

-  Understand  basic  concepts  of  measurements  &amp;  measurement  Systems ,  e.g.  static  and dynamic  characteristics of  instruments, definitions -true value, accuracy, error, precision, sensitivity, and resolution.
-  Get fundamental theory of electric power system ,  e.g.  Effective  Values  of  Voltage  and Current, Idealized Components  Subjected  to  Sinusoidal  Voltages:  Ideal Resistors; Idealized  Capacitors;  and  Idealized  Inductors;  Power  Factor;  The  Power  Triangle  and Power  Factor  Correction;  Three-Wire,  Single-Phase  Residential  Wiring;  Three-Phase Systems: Balanced, Wye-Connected Systems; and Delta-Connected, Three-Phase Systems.
-  Understand  and  use  electromechanical  and  electronic  instruments ,  e.g.  permanentmagnet moving-coil, moving-iron, dynamometer type, induction-type, and electrostatictype instruments, electronic multimeters, digital voltmeters.
-  Understand and use instrument transformer, e.g. current and voltage transformers.
-  Understand and use potentiometers, e.g. principle of D.C. potentiometer, direct reading potentiometers, accurate forms of potentiometers, A.C. potentiometer principle, polar and coordinate type A. C. potentiometer, and applications of A.C. and D.C. potentiometers.
-  Measure resistance in an electric circuit by various methods ,  e.g. measurement of low, medium  &amp;  high  resistances  by  using  Wheatstone  and  Kelvin  bridges,  insulation resistance  measurement,  localization  of  cable  fault  and  loop  tests  by  resistance measurement.
-  Measure inductance and capacitance by different common methods e.g. Maxwell, Hays, Anderson and Owen bridges, capacitance measurement - Desauty and Schering Bridge measurement of frequency by Wien's bridge.
-  Measure and analyze power and energy in electric circuits by indirect and direct methods e.g. use of electrodynamometer-type wattmeter, induction-type energy meter, combination of voltmeters and ammeters, and use of different energy meters.

## Module content:

|   No. | Topics                                          |
|-------|-------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Fundamentals of Measurement and Instrumentation |
|    2. | Fundamentals of Electric Power                  |
|    3. | Measurement Uncertainty                         |

|    5. | Instrument Transformers                         |
|    6. | Analog Electronic Volt-Ohm-Milliameters         |
|    7. | Signal Conditioning                             |
|    8. | Direct-Current Meters and Bridges               |
|    9. | Alternating Current Meters and Bridges          |

|   10. | Potentiometer Circuits and Reference Voltages   |
|-------|-------------------------------------------------|
|   11. | Measurement of Resistance                       |
|   12. | Measurement of Inductance and Capacitance       |
|   13. | Measurements of Power, Power Factor and Energy  |

Prerequisites

Caculus

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

To  provide  the  students  with  the  main  notions  and  techniques  of  calculus  of  functions  of several  variables  concerning  limits,  continuity,  differentiation  and  integration;  basic  skills  of computing  the  sum  of  series,  Fourier  series.  Many  applications  explain  how  to  use  these notions and techniques in practical situations.

1. To provide the students with the main notions and techniques of calculus of functions of several variables concerning limits, continuity, differentiation and integration; basic skills of computing the sum of series, Fourier series. Many applications explain how to use these notions and techniques in practical situations.
2. To provide an understanding of the practical meaning, significance and applications of these ideas and techniques, through practical examples taken from many areas of engineering, business and the life sciences
3. To develop skills in mathematical modelling and problem solving, in thinking logically, and in creatively applying existing knowledge to new situations
4. To develop confidence and fluency in discussing mathematics in English.

|-------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 1.    | Sequences and Series 1. Sequences, convergent and divergent sequences 2. Series, convergent and divergent series 3. Convergent tests for series with positive terms: comparison tests, ratio tests, root tests and integral test 4. Alternating series - alternating series test 5. Absolute and conditional convergence 6. Important series: power series, Taylor and Maclaurin series, Fourier series |
| 2.    | Analytic Geometry of Space 2.1 Euclidean n-spaces 2.2 Vectors in R^3 3. Inner product and Cross product 4. Lines and planes 5. Surfaces                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
|      | Partial Derivatives 1. Sets in R^n 2. Functions of several variables 3. Continuity 4. Partial derivatives 5. Tangent planes and linear approximations                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |

|    | 6. The chain rule 7. Maxima and minima                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
|----|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 4. | Multiple Integrals 1. Doubles integrals over rectangles 2. Iterated integrals 3. Double integrals in polar coordinates 4. Applications of Double Integrals 5. Triple integrals 6. Triple integrals in cylindrical coordinates 7. Triple Integrals in spherical coordinates |
| 5. | Vector Calculus 5.1 Vector Fields 5.2 Line Integrals 5.3 The fundamental theorem for line integrals 5.4 Green's Theorem 5.5 Curl and divergence 5.6 Surface Integrals                                                                                                      |
| 6. | Basic Concepts of Probability Theory 6.1 Outcomes, Events, Probability 6.2 Laplace Experiments and Elementary Combinatorics 6.3 Independence, Conditional Probabilities 6.4 Random variables, mean value, covariance.                                                      |

## Prerequisites

Proficiency  in  multivariable  calculus  and  vector  analysis  equivalent  to  module 61ECE203 Advanced  Engineering  Mathematics .  Knowledge  of  introductory  physics,  including  electrical and magnetic phenomena.

## Applicability for other modules

## 61ECE326 RF Engineering

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the student will be able to:

1. apply the problem-solving process to solve electric and magnetic field problems;
2. use vector fields and vector calculus to describe electric and magnetic fields;
3. analyze static electric fields of arbitrary charge distributions;
4. analyze steady magnetic fields of arbitrary current density distributions;
5. understand  the  various  laws  of  electric  and  magnetic  fields  to  study  electromagnetic fields  and  to  apply  them  to  practical  electromagnetic  field  problems:  Coulomb's  law, Gauss's law, Biot-Savart law, Ampere's circuital law, Faraday's law, etc.;
6. select the most appropriate method for a practical electromagnetic field problem;
7. perform an electromagnetic field analysis to find the desired parameter;
8. apply vector calculus (Divergence, Curl, Gradient) to the study of electromagnetic fields;
9. understand Maxwell's equations and provide a physical interpretation of their relevance to electrical engineering.

|    8. | Capacitance and the Laplace's & Poisson's equations |

|   12. | Magnetic materials                                  |
|   13. | Inductance                                          |
|   14. | Time-varying fields                                 |
