Module title

Analog Signals and Systems

Module code

61ECE205

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer

| Type               | Lecturer           | Email                | Office   | Office hours (if any)   |
|--------------------|--------------------|----------------------|----------|-------------------------|
| Module Coordinator | Dr.-Ing. Udo Klein | udo.klein@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | tbd                     |
| Lecturer           | Dr.-Ing. Udo Klein | udo.klein@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | tbd                     |

Classification

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

Semester

Winter Semester

## Student workload

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites Proficiency  in  differential  and  integral  calculus  and  familiarity  with  complex numbers.  Knowledge  of  the  physics  of  electricity  and  magnetism.  Solid  skills  in  introductory circuit analysis equivalent to module 61ECE116 Electric Circuits .

## Applicability  for  other  modules 61ECE210 Control  Engineering , 61ECE214 Communication Engineering , 61ECE313 Electronic Circuits , 61ECE326 RF Engineering

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the student will be able to:

1. derive and sketch the frequency response of a linear circuit or system;
2. calculate the response of dissipative linear systems to multi-frequency inputs;
3. calculate the Fourier series of a periodic signal;
4. apply the Fourier series concept to calculate the output of a system due to a periodic input;
5. calculate  the  Fourier  transform  of  finite-energy  aperiodic  signals  and  understand  the concepts of signal energy and bandwidth;
6. explain and analyze the concepts of AM  coherent demodulation, noncoherent demodulation, envelope detection, and a complete AM superheterodyne receiver;
7. calculate and visualize convolution and apply the concept of impulse;
8. explain  the  sampling  theorem  and  select  a  sampling  rate  according  to  the  Nyquist criterion;
9. determine whether a system is linear or nonlinear, causal or noncausal, time-invariant or time-varying, and decompose  system  outputs  into zero-input and zero-state components;
10. determine whether a circuit or system is stable or unstable and demonstrate an understanding of the definition of stability;
11. calculate the one-sided Laplace transform and its inverse;
12. apply the concept of impedance to find the transfer function of a circuit;
13. compute transfer functions from block diagrams;
14. explain  the  relationship  between  pole  and  zero  locations  of  a  circuit  and  its corresponding frequency response;
15. design a Butterworth filter having a desired cutoff frequency;
16. map a designed transfer function to a circuit composed of second-order op-amp building blocks.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                             |
|-------|---------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Examples of signals and signal processing systems |
|    2. | Analog linear time-invariant systems              |
|    3. | Circuits and linear systems                       |
|    4. | Frequency response and multi-frequency circuits   |
|    5. | Fourier Series                                    |
|    6. | Fourier transform                                 |

|   7. | AMradio                                                    |
|------|------------------------------------------------------------|
|   8. | Convolution                                                |
|   9. | Impulse and impulse response                               |
|  10. | Sampling theorem and overview of digital signal processing |
|  11. | Stability                                                  |
|  12. | Laplace transform and transfer function                    |
|  13. | Laplace transform solution of differential equations       |
|  14. | General form of solution to a differential equation        |
|  15. | Design of active filters                                   |

Module title

Object Oriented Programming

Module code

61ECE206

Study program

## Student workload

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency

The module is offered each academic year

## Prerequisites

61ECE115 Introduction to Programming is highly recommended

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Master  the  most  important  concepts  and  elements  of  object-oriented  programming: encapsulation,  data  hiding,  inheritance,  polymorphism,  templates,  using  C++  as  the programming language.
2. Provide solutions to given tasks of medium complexity through the process of problem analysis, formulation, implementation, testing, and documentation.
3. Develop and implement data structures using object-oriented programming approach.
4. Work  in  programs  of  medium  to  greater  complexity,  systematically  seek  and  fix programming errors.

## Contents

| No.   | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
|-------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 1.    | C++ Basics  Course introduction.  C++ Basics: data types, operators, variables, references, constness, input/output.  Control flows: branching and iterations.  Preprocessors and conditional compilation.  Header files and header guards. |
|       | Programming Exercise 1                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| 2.    | Pointers and Arrays  Addresses and pointers.  Arrays: one- and multi-dimensional.  Memory allocation                                                                                                                                          |
|       | Programming Exercise 2                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| 3.    | Variables and Functions  Variables: local, global, extern, static.  Call by value vs. Call by reference.  Return types.  Functions: declaration, definition.  Function overloading.  Recursive functions.  Inline functions.              |
|       | Programming Exercise 3                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| 4.    | User-Defined Types: Classes and Objects  Declaration and definition.  Access privilege and data hiding.  Constructors and destructors.  Operator overloading.                                                                                |
|       | Programming Exercise 4                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |

| 5.   | Inheritance and Polymorphism  Access privileges for derived classes  Constructors and destructors  Calling inherited methods  Polymorphism with virtual methods  Abstract classes   |
|------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|      | Programming Exercise 5                                                                                                                                                                   |
| 6.   | Generic Programming  Namespaces  Templates                                                                                                                                             |
|      | Programming Exercise 6                                                                                                                                                                   |
| 7.   | Debugging  Debugging with gdb  Exception handling with try and catch                                                                                                                   |
| 8.   | Final Project Coding  Topics chosen by lecturers  12 - 16 AHs in computer labs  Class presentation (optional)                                                                         |

## Mode of Assessment

Online interaction: The e-learning platform will count the frequency of logging into the site and giving comments.

Programming Exercises (30 marks) During computer lab times, students are expected to work on their programming exercises. They can work by themselves or discuss in group, but have to submit their assignment individually. If any student is absent in which lab, s/he will receive a grade of zero for that exercise.

Final  Project (20  marks)  Students  in  groups  of  two  or  three  spend  approximately  16  AHs  to complete their final project. The marking is based on the completeness of the project and running of the demo program, and/or group presentation.

Penalties for late submission of group project report:

- If the report is submitted up to one calendar week after the original deadline (or any formally agreed extension to the deadline): 10% of the total marks available for the piece of work will be deducted from the mark for each working day (or part thereof) following the deadline up to a total of five working days.
-  If  the  report  is  submitted  more  than  five  working  days  after  the  original  deadline  (or  any formally agreed extension to the deadline): a mark of zero will be recorded.

## Exams

- Length of examination: 90 minutes
- Open examination. All course materials or computer using is allowed.

## Grading policy

| Assessment method         | Percentage of total                 | Assessment date                 |
|---------------------------|-------------------------------------|---------------------------------|
| Lab programming exercises | 30 After each topic                 |                                 |
| 20                        | After the submission presentation   | Final Project or                |
|                           | 50 One week after the last exercise | Final exam/Written exam lecture |
| Total                     | 100                                 |                                 |

## Student workload

| Credits                              |   6 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency Once each academic year

## Prerequisites

Knowledge of 61ECE111 Calculus is an advantage. Learners will be expected to be familiar with DC and AC circuit analysis.

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Acquire a basic knowledge in solid state electronics including diodes, MOSFET, BJT, and operational amplifier.
2. Demonstrate capacity to  analyze,  simulate  and  design  analog  electronic  circuits  using discrete and VLSI components.
3. Design,  construct,  and  take  measurements  of  various  analog  circuits  to  compare experimental results in the laboratory with theoretical analysis.
4. Demonstrate  capacity  to  apply  the  analog  circuit  theories  to  sensing  and  biomedical applications.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
|-------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Semiconductor basics  Band theory of solids  Intrinsic conductivity  Doping  Diffusion currents in semiconductors                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
|    2. | Semiconductor diode and applications  The pn-junction  pn-junction with zero bias  pn-junction with bias  small-signal model of a pn-junction  spice model of a semiconductor diode  different types of semiconductor diodes  Diode applications  Diode as rectifier  Voltage multiplier  Zener diode as voltage regulator |
|    3. | The bipolar junction transistor and applications  The bipolar junction transistor  Structure and operation principles of a pnp BJT  Static input and output characteristics of a BJT  Simple small signal BJT model                                                                                                              |

4.

5.

-  Advanced small signal BJT model
-  SPICE model of a BJT
-  Small signal amplifier
-  BJT biasing
-  Common-emitter amplifier
-  Common-collector amplifier
-  Integrated circuit techniques
-  The different amplifier
-  Current sources
-  Active load
-  Level-shifting circuits
-  Complementary output stage
-  Design of Gilbert multipliers
-  Design of mixers

## Field-effect transistors and their applications

-  Junction field-effect transistor
-  Cross-section and static IU-characteristic of a JFET
-  Small signal equivalent circuit of a JFET
-  SPICE model of a JFET
-  Common-source small signal amplifier with a JFET
-  Metal-oxide semiconductor field-effect transistor (MOSFET)
-  N-channel MOSFET
-  P-channel MOSFET
-  Static characteristics of a n-channel enhancement MOSFET
-  Small signal equivalent circuit of a n-channel MOSFET
-  SPICE model of a MOSFET
-  Common-source small signal amplifier with an n-channel MOSFET

## Operational amplifiers and their applications

-  Basic linear model of an operational amplifier
-  Basic linear op-amp circuits
-  Inverting amplifier
-  Inverting summing amplifier
-  Non-inverting amplifier
-  Inverting integrator
-  Inverting differentiator
-  First-order low-pass filter
-  Second-order low-pass filter
-  Band-pass filters
-  Multiple feedback bandpass filters.
-  Basic non-linear op-amp circuits
-  Op-amp as comparator
-  Schmitt trigger realized with an op-amp
-  Digital-to-analog converter (DAC)
-  Op-amp summer as DAC
-  DAC with R-2R-Ladder network
-  Analog-to-digital converter (ADC)
-  Quantization error
-  ADC realizations

## VLSI Design

-  Use of MAGIC and LAZI
-  Full-custom Designs of
-  Bipolar components
6.  CMOS components
-  BICMOS components
-  Place and Route
-  Design rule checks, including DRC, ERC and LVS

Module title

Digital System Design

Module code

61ECE208

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer

| Type               | Lecturer                   | Email                 | Office   | Office hours (if any)   |
|--------------------|----------------------------|-----------------------|----------|-------------------------|

Classification

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

Semester

Summer Semester

## Student workload

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency The module is offered each academic year.

## Prerequisites None

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Describe, derive, and simplify combinational logic expression using tools and theorems in order to design and troubleshoot a correspondent logic circuit.
2. Understand the principles of and combine logic gates in different integrated circuits (IC).
3. Understand, describe, and use different numerical systems such as binary, decimal, hexadecimal, binary-coded decimal (BCD) systems in designing logic and arithmetic circuits.
4. Understand manufacturers' data sheets, low voltage technology, open-collector outputs, tristate devices, IC interfacing, mixed-voltage interfacing, and troubleshooting using a logic pulser and a logic probe.
5. Analyze and use decoders and encoders, LEDs and LCDs, multiplexers and demultiplexers, understand data busing.
6. Understand digital-to-analog (DACs) and analog-to-digital converters (ADCs).
7. Understand how memories work, know different characteristics, and compare memories and combine memory ICs.
8. Understand how PLD works, describe categories and compare different types of PLDs.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                    |
|-------|----------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Number Systems and Codes                                 |
|    2. | Combinational Logic Circuits                             |
|    3. | Flip-Flops and Digital Arithmetics                       |
|    4. | Counters and registers                                   |
|    5. | Integrated-circuit logic families and MSI logic circuits |
|    6. | Memory device                                            |
|    7. | Programmable logic device architectures                  |

## Lab

## Exams (80%)

-  Printed and written materials are allowed.
-  All electronic devices are NOT allowed except individual calculator.

Digital Signal Processing

Module code

61ECE209

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Student workload

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|

| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered once per academic year

## Prerequisites

-  Proficiency  in  fundamentals  of  engineering  mathematics:  differential  equations,  difference equations, complex exponential.
-  Familiar  with  basic  concepts  of  analog  signals  and  systems  such  as  continuous  Fourier transform, Laplace transform, Laplace transfer function, system response and signal analysis of circuits.

## Applicability for other modules

Relates to the modules Control Engineering, Communications Engineering

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Recognize the terminology that is used in the Digital Signal Processing (DSP) field.
2. Explain the theory and concepts behind the construction of DSP systems.
3. Analyze basic DSP building blocks; including analog-to-digital (A/D) and digital-to-analog (D/A) converters, digital filters, spectrum analyzers, sample rate converters (up-sampling and down-sampling), and the fast Fourier transform (FFT) algorithm.
4. Design and synthesize these building blocks and use them effectively in applications.
5. Think critically, ask questions, and apply problem-solving techniques.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
|-------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Overview of digital signal processing Basic concepts and applications.                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
|    2. | Discrete-time signals and systems Continuous-time vs. discrete-time signal. Discrete-time system: linearity, shift- invariance, causality, stability criteria. Linear shift-invariant system. System representation using difference equation. Convolution and unit-pulse response. |
|    3. | The z-transform Definition and properties. Inverse z-transform , region of convergence, poles and zeros. Convolution via z-transform. Solution of difference equation using z- transform. System BIBO stability.                                                                    |
|    4. | Frequency analysis of signals                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |

|    | Discrete-time Fourier Transform and its properties. Discrete Fourier Transform and its properties. Cyclic shifting and cyclic convolution. DFT spectral analysis.                        |
|----|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 5. | Frequency analysis of linear shift-time invariant systems System frequency response. Eigen property of linear shift-time invariant systems. Phase of frequency response and group delay. |
| 6. | Sampling and reconstruction of signals Analog frequency response of a digital processor. Ideal sampling and reconstruction. Nyquist sampling theorem. Non-ideal D/A converters.          |
| 7. | Digital Filters Digital filter structure and block diagram. FIR versus IIR filters. Filter design using windowing method.                                                                |
| 8. | Review                                                                                                                                                                                   |

Module title

Control Engineering

Module code

61ECE210

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer

| Type               | Lecturer             | Email               | Office   | Office hours (if any)   |
|--------------------|----------------------|---------------------|----------|-------------------------|
| Module Coordinator | Dr. Tran Trung Thanh | thanh.tt@vgu.edu.vn | B109     | 2:00-4:00 PM, Wed       |
| Lecturer           | Dr. Tran Trung Thanh | thanh.tt@vgu.edu.vn | B109     | 2:00-4:00 PM, Wed       |
| Lab                | Mr. Vo Van Phung     | phung.vv@vgu.edu.vn | B.111    | None                    |

Classification

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

## Semester Summer Semester

## Student workload

|   Credits | 5   | ECTS                                 |
|-----------|-----|--------------------------------------|
|        60 | AHs | Contact hours (Lecture + Labs)       |
|        90 | AHs | Assignments and independent learning |
|       150 | AHs | Total Working hours                  |

Frequency The module is offered each academic year

## Prerequisites

61ECE108 Linear algebra; 61ECE203 Advanced Engineering Mathematics; 61ECE111 Introduction to Programming

## Applicability for other modules

61ECE306 Smart Systems in Automation; 61ECE318 Robotics &amp; Autonomous  Systems; 61ECE316 Industrial Automation; 61ECE404 Bachelor-Thesis

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Understand  history,  current  developments,  trends,  and  basic  knowledge  of  modern control engineering;
2. Model  simple  and  moderately  complex  control  systems  using  transfer  functions  and state-space time domain descriptions;
3. Analyze the stability of a single input single output linear control system;
4. Design  feedback  controllers  using  root  locus,  frequency  domain,  and  state-space techniques to achieve a desired transient response and acceptable steady-state errors;
5. Understand basis, principles and methods for control analysis and design of nonlinear dynamic systems. Know how to use and apply structures of feedback systems such as feedforward  control,  cascade  control;  control  design  of  feedback  linearization  for nonlinear dynamic systems.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
|-------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Introduction to control system Introduction; Example of control systems; closed-loop vs. open-loop control; Design and Compensation of control systems.                                                   |
|    2. | Mathematical modelling of control system Transfer function model; state-space model; Linearization of nonlinear dynamic systems; Examples of engineering system: Mechanical and electrical systems.       |
|    3. | Transient and Steady-State Response Analyses First-order system, second-order system, transient response analysis with MATLAB, Routh's stability criterion; Steady-state error in unity -feedback control |

|     | system; Examples.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
|-----|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|  4. | Control System Analysis and Design by the Root-locus Method Root-locus plots; plotting root-loci with MATLAB; Root-locus approach to control system design: lead compensation, lag compensation, lag-lead compensation; examples;                                           |
|  5. | Control System Analysis and Design by the Frequency-Response Method Bode diagram; log-Magnitude vs phase plots; Nyquist stability criterion; stability analysis; control design by frequency-response approach : lead compensation, lag compensation, lag-lead compensation |
|  6. | PID control and Applications Introduction and application of PID controller; Ziegler-Nichols Rules for tuning PID controller; Design of PID controller with frequency-response approach; Examples                                                                           |
|  7. | Control System Analysis and Design in State space State-space representation of transfer function systems; Transformation of system models with MATHLAB; Controllability; Observability; Pole Placement; Solving Pole-Placement Problems with MATHLAB;                      |
|  8. | Introduction to nonlinear control/dynamic systems Why is Nonlinear Control? Some Concepts; Properties of Nonlinear Systems; Analysis and Design methods; Research Trends                                                                                                    |
|  9. | Analysis of nonlinear dynamic systems Phase plane analysis, Lyapunov theory, advanced stability theory                                                                                                                                                                      |
| 10. | Traditional methods for design of nonlinear control system Linear control design using the state space model and feedback control; Gain scheduling; feedback linearization with several examples                                                                            |

Assignments: 5 assignments. Submission of each assignment gets 2 marks.

Group project (10 marks) Criteria to get maximum grade or excellent group project report. Penalties for late submission of group project report:

- If the report is submitted up to one calendar week after the original deadline (or any formally agreed extension to the deadline): 10% of the total marks available for the piece of work will be deducted from the mark for each working day (or part thereof) following the deadline up to a total of five working days.
-  If  the  report  is  submitted  more  than  five  working  days  after  the  original  deadline  (or  any formally agreed extension to the deadline): a mark of zero will be recorded.

Module title

Fundamentals of Power Engineering

Module code

61ECE212

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type    | Lecturer                               | Email   | Office                     | Office hours (if any)   |
|---------|----------------------------------------|---------|----------------------------|-------------------------|
| Lecture | Dr. Bui Minh Duong duong.bm@vgu.edu.vn | B111    | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon and Fri |                         |
| Lab     | Van Phung phung.vv@vgu.edu.vn          | B107    | None                       | Mr. Vo                  |

Classification:

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

Semester:

Summer Semester

## Student workload:

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites: 61ECE116

Electric Circuits

Applicability  for  other  modules: 61ECE301 Electric  Machines ; 61ECE323 Electric  Motors and Drives ; 61ECE320 Drives  in  Automation ;  and  other  modules  related  to  a  major  of  Energy Technology (ET)

## Duration: 15 weeks Course description:

This course introduces different energy sources and electric energy conversion techniques. The course  specifically  presents  an  overview  of  the  electric  power  system  and  its  components, reviews  power  concepts  in  electrical  circuits,  and  covers  magnetic  circuits  and  transformers, fundamentals  of  rotating  machines,  theory  and  application  of  three-phase  and  single-phase induction  machines,  and  theory  and  application  of  DC  machines.  Problems,  examples, illustrations and diagrams are also included in the course.

## Intended learning outcomes:

Students understand basic aspects of operation and control of electromagnetic power system under both steady-state and rotating conditions. They achieve basic knowledge of functioning conditions, operating behavior and interaction of energy supply equipment. Specifically, on the successful completion of this module, the learner will be able to:

-  Get fundamental theory of magnetic circuits and magnetic materials;
-  Understand principles of Electromechanical-Energy-Conversion systems;
-  Know configurations and operating principles of power transformers; and do theoretical analysis and no-load and short-circuit experiments of transformers;
-  Use equivalent circuits to analyze basic characteristics of power transformers, e.g. noload,  short-circuit  and  normal  operation  conditions  of  transformers,  and  parallel operation of transformers.
-  Know configurations and explain the operating principles of induction machines and DC machines;
-  Do theoretical analysis and experiments of induction machines and DC machines;
-  Know how to start and operate these machines e.g. using different indirect and direct methods to start DC and AC machines and operation of the machines at transient and steady-state conditions.
-  Use  equivalent  circuits  to  explain  basic  characteristics  of  AC  and  DC  machines,  e.g. starting  methods  of  the  machines  and  no-load  and  short-circuit  experiments  of  the machines.

## Contents :

|    4. | AC Machinery Fundamentals                                    |
|    5. | Induction Motors (IMs)                                       |
|    6. | Single-Phase Induction Motors                                |
|    7. | DC Machinery Fundamentals                                    |
|    8. | DC Motors and Generators                                     |

Module title

Electric Power Grids

Module code

61ECE213

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type    | Lecturer                               | Email   | Office                     | Office hours (if any)   |
|---------|----------------------------------------|---------|----------------------------|-------------------------|
| Lecture | Dr. Bui Minh Duong duong.bm@vgu.edu.vn | B111    | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon and Fri |                         |
| Lab     | Phung phung.vv@vgu.edu.vn              | B107    | None                       | Mr. Vo Van              |

Classification:

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

## Semester: Summer Semester at Binh Duong campus/TBC Student workload:

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites: 61ECE116 Electric Circuits

Applicability for other modules: 61ECE311 Renewable Energy Systems 1 , 61ECE321 Renewable Energy Systems 2 ,s 61ECE309 Power System Analysis ; and 61ECE308 Smart Grids

Duration:

## 15 weeks

## Course description:

This course presents an overview of electric power system and its components, reviews power concepts in electrical circuits, and covers magnetic circuits and power transformers. Moreover, the course also introduces fundamental theory of DC and AC machines, appropriate models of the  main  components  in  an  interconnected  power  system  (e.g.  models  of  lines,  generators, cables, transformers and loads). Matlab software is used to perform necessary calculations on admittance and impedance models of a power system. Problems, examples, illustrations and diagrams are also included in the course.

## Intended learning outcomes:

Upon completion of this module, students can be able to:

-  Understand  the  concepts  of  power  factor  angle,  power  factor,  complex  power,  and conservation of power;
-  Solve  single-phase  circuits  for  the  real,  reactive,  and  complex  power  supplied  by  or consumed by any device in the circuit;
-  Solve simple three-phase circuits to calculate any system voltage, current, or power;
-  Understand and use per-phase analysis to solve the simple three-phase systems;
-  Know configurations and operating principles of power transformers; and do theoretical analysis and no-load and short-circuit experiments of transformers;
-  Use equivalent circuits to analyze basic characteristics of power transformers, e.g. noload,  short-circuit  and  normal  operation  conditions  of  transformers,  and  parallel operation of transformers;
-  Apply concepts from basic electromagnetics to determine the inductance, capacitance, and resistance of three-phase transmission lines;
-  Do the basic design of transmission lines to specified parameters;
-  Derive the relationships between the voltage and current on a transmission line, and use hyperbolic functions to solve for the voltage or current at any point along the line;
-  Calculate the bus-admittance/bus-impedance matrix for a three-phase system consisting of transmission lines, transformers and capacitors by writing a basic computer program using Matlab software;

Module title

Communications Engineering

Module code

61ECE214

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer

| Type               | Lecturer                 | Email               | Office   | Office hours (if any)   |
|--------------------|--------------------------|---------------------|----------|-------------------------|
| Module Coordinator | Dr. Thai Truyen Dai Chan | chan.ttd@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | 9am-11am, Mon-Fri       |
| Lecturer           | Dr. Thai Truyen Dai Chan | chan.ttd@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | 9am-11am, Mon-Fri       |
| Lab                | Msc. Tran Quang Nhu      | nhu.tq@vgu.edu.vn   | B.101    | 9am-11am, Mon-Fri       |

Classification

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

Semester

Summer Semester

## Student workload

| Credits 5ECTS                              |
|--------------------------------------------|
| Contact hours 60AHs                        |
| Assignments and independent learning 90AHs |
| Total Working hours 150AHs                 |

Frequency The module is offered each academic year.

## Prerequisites

1. Calculus
2. Linear Algebra

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Understand the functionalities of main parts of a communication system;
2. Understand  the  basis,  principle  and  methods  of  transmission  technology,  such  as modulation/demodulation techniques, and detection techniques;
3. Understand the behavior of basic wireless communication channels;
4. Know basic concepts in information theory;
5. Know the principles of linear block codes, trellis and graph based codes, and fluent in designing a few types of them;
6. Design and evaluate the performance of a complete communication system.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                 |
|-------|---------------------------------------|
|    1. | Introduction of communication systems |

|   2. | Mathematical background for Signal analysis   |
|------|-----------------------------------------------|
|   3. | Digital Modulation Schemes                    |
|   4. | Optimum Receivers forAWGN Channels            |
|   5. | Introduction to Information Theory            |
|   6. | Linear Block Codes                            |
|   7. | Trellis and Graph Based Codes                 |

## Learning activities

| Activities   | Explanation                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
|--------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Exercises    | Students work on a few typical exercises of each lecture in the class. One student volunteers to present each exercise on the board.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| Group work   | Each group work on a project and present in the class.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| Self-study   | Students read materials and work on exercises at home.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| Lab The      | course includes 4 lab exercises on Modulation and Transmission Technology as follows  Transmitting Technology: Double single sideband, single sideband;  Receiving Technology: Tuned frequency receiver, PLL;  Modem Technology: Modulation/Demodulation, RZ, NRZ, ASK, FSK;  Telecommunication Lines: Fiber optical attenuation, bending loss, fiber-to-fiber coupling. |

## Mode of Assessment

## Group project with Presentation (10%)

-  All topics of the projects are registered by students at the beginning of the module and the tentative date of the presentation of each group determined.

## Lab

-  A  student  need  to  register,  participate  in,  and  pass  the  lab  in  order  to  be  eligible  for participating in the final exam.

Module title

Electric Machines

Module code

61ECE301

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type    | Lecturer                               | Email   | Office                     | Office hours (if any)   |
|---------|----------------------------------------|---------|----------------------------|-------------------------|
| Lecture | Dr. Bui Minh Duong duong.bm@vgu.edu.vn | B111    | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon and Fri |                         |
| Lab     | Phung phung.vv@vgu.edu.vn              | B107    | None                       | Mr. Vo Van              |

Classification:

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

Semester:

Winter Semester

## Student workload:

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites: 61ECE116

Electric Circuits

Applicability  for  other  modules:

61ECE323 Electric  Motors  and  Drives ;

61ECE320 Drives  in

Automation

; and other modules related to a major of Energy Technology (ET)

Duration:

15 weeks

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

## Course description:

The  course  is  to  teach  operating  principles  of  DC  and  AC  motors  and  generators,  practical analytical  models  (equivalent  circuit  diagrams)  for  most  types  of  motors  and  generators commonly used in industry, and power capability, efficiency, operating characteristics, control requirements,  and  electrical  demands  of  these  machines.  This  course  also  presents  starting methods  of  DC  and  AC  machines  and  common  speed  and  torque  control  methods  of  these machines. Moreover, structures, operating principles, control systems and theoretical calculations of special motors such as servo motors, stepper motors, permanent magnet and brushless DC motors are introduced in this course.

## Intended learning outcomes:

After successful completing the course, the students can be able to:

-  Explain  the  operating  principles  of  induction  machines,  synchronous  machines,  DC machines  and  other  special  motors,  such  as  servo  motors,  stepping  motors  and reluctance motors;
-  Identify parameters in models of the electrical machines;
-  Use equivalent circuits to analyze electrical machines in the steady state;
-  Construct phasor diagrams for different loads and to use the vector method for analysis of AC machines;
-  Describe  the  design  process  of  a  simple  three-phase  ac  winding  and  explain  the concepts of pole number and winding factor;
-  Explain the background to voltage and current harmonics and estimate their influence on power losses in electrical machines;
-  Know  how  to  simply  control  speed  and  torque  of  DC  Motors;  synchronous  motors; induction motors; servo motors, stepping motors and reluctance motors;

## Contents :

|   No. | Topics                                             |
|-------|----------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Lecture 1 - AC Machinery Fundamentals              |
|    2. | Lecture 2 - Synchronous Generators                 |
|    3. | Lecture 3 - Synchronous Motors                     |
|    4. | Lecture 4 - Induction Motors (IMs)                 |
|    5. | Lecture 5 - Single- and Two-Phase Induction Motors |
|    6. | Lecture 6 - DC Machinery Fundamentals              |
|    7. | Lecture 7 - DC Motors and Generators               |

|   8. | Lecture 8 - Speed and Torque Control   |
|------|----------------------------------------|
|   9. | Lecture 9 - Special Machines           |

## Integrity:

Academic dishonesty is a completely unacceptable mode of conduct and will not be tolerated in any form. All  persons involved in academic dishonesty will be disciplined in accordance with University regulations and procedures. Discipline may include suspension or expulsion from the University. 'Scholastic dishonesty includes but is not limited to cheating, plagiarism, collusion, and the submission for credit of any work or materials that are attributable in whole or in part to another person, taking an examination for another person, any act designed to give unfair advantage to a student or the attempt to commit such acts.'

Module title

Machine Learning

Module code

61ECE302

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer

| Type               | Lecturer                 | Email               | Office   | Office hours (if any)   |
|--------------------|--------------------------|---------------------|----------|-------------------------|
| Module Coordinator | Dr. Thai Truyen Dai Chan | chan.ttd@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | 9am-11am, Mon-Fri       |
| Lecturer Dr. Chan  | Thai Truyen Dai          | chan.ttd@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | 9am-11am, Mon-Fri       |
| Lab                | Bien Minh Tri            | tri.bm@vgu.edu.vn   | B.       | 9am-11am, Mon-Fri       |

Classification

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

Semester

Winter Semester

## Student workload

| Credits                              | 5ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|---------|
| Contact hours                        | 60AHs   |
| Assignments and independent learning | 90AHs   |
| Total Working hours                  | 150AHs  |

Frequency The module is offered each academic year.

Prerequisites None

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Know and understand the  working  methods of  machine-learning  systems  and  master the basics of the methods used;
2. Have problem-solving skills for problems that can be handled with machine learning and can assess whether such a solution can be used for a practical underlying problem;
3. Describe the basics of supervised and unsupervised learning;
4. Use linear methods for regression and classifications;
5. Describe  basic  principles  of  expansions  and  regularization,  and  Kernel  smoothing methods;
6. Know how to fit and train neural networks.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic        |
|-------|--------------|
|    1. | Introduction |

|   2. | Supervised Learning Variable types; statistical decision theory; local methods; structured regression models.                                              |
|------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|   3. | Linear Methods for Regression Linear regression models and least squares; subset selection; shrinkage methods; and methods using derived input directions. |
|   4. | Linear Methods for Classifications Regression of an indicator matrix; discriminant analysis; and logistic regression.                                      |
|   5. | Basic Expansions and Regularization Piecewise polynomials and splines; filtering and feature extraction; and smoothing splines.                            |
|   6. | Kernel Smoothing Methods One-directional Kernel smoothers; selecting the width of the Kernel; and local likelihood and other models.                       |
|   7. | Neural Networks Projection pursuit regression; fitting and training neural networks.                                                                       |
|   8. | Unsupervised Learning Association rules; cluster analysis; and principal components, curves and surfaces.                                                  |

## Learning activities

| Activities   | Explanation                                                                                                                                                            |
|--------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Exercises    | Students work on a few typical exercises of each lecture in the class. One student volunteers to present each exercise on the board.                                   |
| Group work   | Each group work on a project and present in the class.                                                                                                                 |
| Self-study   | Students read materials and work on exercises at home.                                                                                                                 |
| Lab          | The course includes 3 lab sessions as follows:  Octave/Matlab goal: basic Matlab/Octave+ data generation;  Local methods: K-NN, PWfor classification;  Lab Kernels. |

## Lab

-  A  student  need  to  register,  participate  in,  and  pass  the  lab  in  order  to  be  eligible  for participating in the final exam.

## Exams (90%)

-  Length of examination: 90 minutes.
-  Printed and written materials are allowed.
-  All electronic devices are NOT allowed except individual calculator.

## Prerequisites None

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Understand the foundation of computer networks emphasized on Internet;
2. Design and analysis a computer network;
3. Describe in detail the working principles of each layer in the OSI model and important protocols such as DNS, TCP, UDP, IP, CSMA/CS;
4. Design protocols for different layers of Internet;
5. Know working principles of wireless LAN;
6. Design and program a network software.

|    5. | Data-link layer: links, access, networks, and LANs |
|    6. | Wireless and mobile networks                       |

Energy Conversion Systems

15 weeks

## Course description:

This  course  introduces  power  electronics  and  renewable  and  distributed  energy  systems, consisting of discussing power-electronic converters topologies, controls, and grid-integration of  renewable  and  distributed  energy  system  applications.  An  overview  of  power-electronic technologies  is  followed  by  the  introduction  of  various  renewable  and  distributed  energy resources  that  includes  photovoltaics,  wind,  small  hydroelectric,  fuel-cells,  micro-turbines, electric  vehicles,  and  variable  speed  generation  systems.  Energy  storage  systems  such  as battery  and  fast  response  storage  systems  are  discussed  along  with  application-specific examples.  The  course,  moreover,  focuses  on  more  complex  topics  such  as  modular  power electronics, microgrids and smart grids for integrating renewable and distributed energy.

## Intended learning outcomes:

After the successful completion of this course, the students can be able to:

-  Get  the  advanced  knowledge  of  converter  topologies  that  are  required  for  the  gridconnected operation mode of renewable energy sources, particularly for photovoltaics, wind, small hydroelectric, fuel-cells, micro-turbines, electric vehicles, and variable speed generation systems.
-  Apply  different  control  methods  of  power  converters  to  control  power,  frequency, voltage, and current in photovoltaic generation systems, wind generation systems, fuelcells, micro-turbines and variable speed generation systems;
-  Analyze  the  operation  and  control  of  power  electronic  topologies  for  EV  and  PHEV charging, Vehicle-to-Grid (V2G), and Vehicle-to-Home (V2H) Concepts;
-  Understand  the  Microgrid  concept:  definitions  and  operating  modes  of  DC  and  AC microgrids;
-  Analyze and select power electronic topologies properly for smart distribution grids;

3.

Module title

Smart Grids

Module code

61ECE308

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type    | Lecturer                               | Email   | Office                     | Office hours (if any)   |
|---------|----------------------------------------|---------|----------------------------|-------------------------|
| Lecture | Dr. Bui Minh Duong duong.bm@vgu.edu.vn | B111    | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon and Fri |                         |
| Lab     | phung.vv@vgu.edu.vn                    | B107    | None                       | Mr. Vo Van Phung        |

Classification:

- [ ] ☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

Semester:

Winter Semester

## Student workload:

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites: 61ECE116 Electric Circuits

Duration:

15 weeks

## Course description:

This  course  is  to  supply  the  basic  knowledge  for  students  to  differentiate  conventional  and smart  grids;  to  identify  the  need  of  Smart  Grid  (SG),  Microgrid  (MG),  Smart  Metering  (SM), Home  Energy  Management  System  (HEMS),  and  Smart  Communication  (SC);  to  get  new upcoming  concepts  in electricity  from  the utility  to  customers;  to  compare  emerging technologies  and  current  professional  issues  in  smart  grids;  and  finally  to  understand  the necessity  of  communication  systems  and  standards  for  smart  grids.  Main  contents  of  this course  are:  (i)  introduction  to  smart  grid  technologies,  ICT  in  the  smart  grid,  and  smart  grid applications; (ii) smart generation systems; (iii) smart distribution and transmission networks; (iv)  smart  grid  measurement  technologies;  (v)  communication-network  architecture  for  the smart grid; (vi) home energy management system; and (vii) computational tools for the smart grid design.

## Intended learning outcomes:

Upon the completion of this course, the students can be able to:

-  Understand  basic  concepts  of  smart  grid  (e.g.  demand  response,  community-based battery  storage,  virtual  power  plants,  advanced  metering  systems,  smart  loads  and appliances) compared with conventional electric grids, and identify its opportunities and barriers;
-  Understand  the  concepts  of  Smart  Metering  (SM),  Smart  Appliances  (SA),  Automatic Meter  Reading/Advanced  Metering  Infrastructure  (AMR/AMI),  Outage  Management System, Smart Sensors, and Home &amp; Building Automation;
-  Understand  the  concepts  of  Substation  Automation,  Feeder  Automation,  Intelligent Electronic  Devices  (IED),  Wide  Area  Measurement  System,  and  Phase  Measurement Unit;
-  Describe  how  information  and  communication  technology  (ICT)  in  combination  with power  electronics  impact  the  profiles  and  methods  of  generation,  transmission, distribution and consumption of electric energy;
-  Apply  several  differently  computational  tools  to  design  a  smart  grid  (e.g.  Classical Optimization Methods -Linear Programming. Nonlinear Programming, Integer Programming, Dynamic Programming; Heuristic Optimization -Artificial Neural Networks  (ANN),  Expert  Systems  (ES);  and  Evolutionary  Computational  Techniques  Genetic Algorithm (GA), Particle Swarm Optimization (PSO), and Ant Colony Optimization);

Module title

Power System Analysis

Module code

61ECE309

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type   | Lecturer                               | Email   | Office                     | Office hours (if any)   |
|--------|----------------------------------------|---------|----------------------------|-------------------------|

| Lab    | Mr. Vo Van Phung phung.vv@vgu.edu.vn   | B107    |                            | None                    |

Semester:

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

Winter Semester

## Student workload:

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites: 61ECE116 Electric Circuits

Applicability for other modules:

61ECE311 Renewable Energy Systems 1 , 61ECE321

Renewable Energy Systems 2 , and 61ECE308 Smart Grids

Duration:

15 weeks

## Course description:

This  course  introduces  the  main  components  and  power  flow  analysis  in  electrical networks. The course also supplies the basic understanding of symmetrical and unsymmetrical faults in the power system and applies theory on symmetrical components and the per-unit to do shortcircuit  analysis  in  the  system.  Protection  fundamentals  and  basic  design  principles  of  a protection system are also presented. The course briefly discusses transient stability cases and control  systems  in  the  power  system.  Moreover,  programs  written  by  Matlab  software  and Power  World  Simulator  software  are  introduced  to  support  for  power-flow  calculations  and fault analysis in the system.

## Intended learning outcomes:

Upon completion of this module, students will be able to:

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

-  Calculate the bus-admittance matrix for a three-phase system consisting of transmission lines, transformers, and capacitors;
-  Formulate the power flow problem and develop a solution algorithm using both the Gauss-Seidel and Newton-Raphson methods to calculate power flows in the power system;
-  Write a simple power-flow calculation program using the Gauss-Seidel method and the Newton-Raphson method due to Matlab software;
-  Calculate fault voltages and currents in a network experiencing a balanced three-phase fault at any location;
-  Understand  the  advantage  of  symmetrical  components  to  analyze  the  unbalanced system  operation;  analyze  positive,  negative,  and  zero  sequence  networks  for  the system  consisting  of  machines,  transmission  lines  and  transformers;  and  solve  fault voltages and currents for single-line to ground faults, line-to-line faults, and double-line to ground faults;
-  Simulate the operation of power system using Power World Simulator software;
-  Understand the main control systems (frequency and voltage) of electric power systems through appropriate mathematical models;
-  Understand state-of-the-art protective techniques and protection applications; and the basic concepts of overcurrent protection, directional/non-directional protection, differential protection, distance  protection,  and  over/under  voltage  &amp;  frequency protection to design a basic protection system for the power system;

Module title

Energy Policy

Module code

61ECE310

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type   | Lecturer                               | Email   | Office                     | Office hours (if any)   |
|--------|----------------------------------------|---------|----------------------------|-------------------------|
|        | Dr. Bui Minh Duong duong.bm@vgu.edu.vn | B111    | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon and Fri | Lecture                 |

Classification:

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

Semester:

Winter Semester

## Student workload:

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites:

None

Applicability for other modules:

61ECE308 Smart Grids

Duration:

15 weeks

## Course description:

This course introduces energy policies to the production and use of different energy sources, along with the management of its energy infrastructure. The goal of the course is to gain an understanding  of  policies  currently  in  place,  as  well  as  proposals  for  alternatives,  while examining the economic, environmental, national security and energy security implications of different  policy  approaches.  The  course  mainly  consists  of  lectures,  discussions,  and  smallgroup work to explore topics such as: tax incentives for renewable energy sources, how policy determines the market for renewable energy, governance of the electrical grid by federal and state  authorities,  the  potential  for  greater  energy  efficiency,  costs  and  benefits  of  different energy sources, and how the national security and environmental impacts of energy usage have spurred policy changes.

## Intended learning outcomes:

## Students who complete this course can be able to:

-  Analyze  and  evaluate  the  potential  economic  and  environmental  impacts  of  different energy policy options involving oil and electricity generation;
-  Explain  and  evaluate  the  benefits  and  drawbacks  of  different  energy  sources  and technologies such as wind, geothermal, solar, biomass and other renewables;
-  Demonstrate  comprehensive  knowledge  of  the  sources  and  volumes  of  current  and projected energy production and usage from renewable resources such as solar, wind and biomass;
-  Develop  the  ability  to  understand  and  navigate  energy  information  reports  and databases;
-  Comprehend trends in the energy sector involving the  financing  of  renewable  energy projects;
-  Develop the ability to write strong, clear and compelling policy briefs;

3.

Module title

Renewable Energy Systems 1

Module code

61ECE311

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type    | Lecturer           | Email               | Office   | Office hours (if any)      |
|---------|--------------------|---------------------|----------|----------------------------|
| Lecture | Dr. Bui Minh Duong | duong.bm@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon and Fri |
| Lab     | Mr. Vo Van Phung   | phung.vv@vgu.edu.vn | B107     | None                       |

Classification:

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

Semester:

Winter Semester

Student workload:

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites: 61ECE116 Electric Circuits

Applicability for other modules: 61ECE321 Renewable Energy Systems 2 and 61ECE308 Smart Grids

Duration:

15 weeks

## Course description:

This  course  provides  an  overview  of  key  technologies  and  methods  for  implementing  power electronic circuits in alternative energy systems for the optimal power generation (e.g. circuits of  DC/DC  converters,  DC/AC  inverters,  and  AC/DC  rectifiers).  The  course  also  supplies  basic knowledge of configurations, operation and control systems of PV and wind-turbine generating systems and introduces how to design of these PV and wind generation systems. The course covers wind and solar applications, as well as tidal, ocean and geothermal energy sources, fuel cells  and  biomass  energy  sources.  Besides  that,  basic  concepts  and  key  technologies  of  a microgrid,  operation  and  control  strategies  of  the  microgrid  as  well  as  the  integration  of microgrid to the utility grid are discussed in this course.

## Intended learning outcomes:

On successful completion of this module, the learner will be able to:

-  Understand the operation and control of DC/DC converters, DC/AC inverters, and AC/DC power rectifiers integrated in renewable-energy generating systems;
-  Calculate and design renewable-energy based generation systems such as PV and windturbine generation systems;
-  Understand  and  analyze  different  energy  conversion  systems  such  as:  solar  thermal conversion  systems;  geothermal,  biomass,  ocean,  tidal-based  energy  sources;  and  fuel cells;
-  Design photovoltaic/wind-turbine microgrid generating stations;

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

-  Understand concepts and technologies of AC and DC microgrids; operation and control of microgrids at grid-connected and islanded operation modes; integration of microgrids to the utility grid; and anti-islanding;
-  Classify and assess the current significance and potential of renewable energies to apply procedures for planning and designing renewable energy systems;
-  Get  presentation  and  teamwork  skills  and  time-management  skills  for  the  on-time submission of assignments;

## Contents :

|   No. | Topics                                                                        |
|-------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Introduction to electrical energy systems                                     |
|    2. | Components of electric energy systems                                         |
|    3. | Fundamentals of Power Electronic Circuits                                     |
|    4. | Microgrid Solar Energy Systems: Configuration and Design                      |
|    5. | Configurations, Operation and Control of PV Generating system                 |
|    6. | Wind Power Systems: Configuration, Operation, Control and Design              |
|    7. | Hydroelectricity                                                              |
|    8. | Fuel cells                                                                    |
|    9. | Geothermal energy                                                             |
|   10. | Ocean thermal energy conversion (OTEC)                                        |
|   11. | Tidal energy                                                                  |
|   12. | Solar thermal energy conversion systems (STECS)                               |
|   13. | Utilization of bio-resources as fuels and energy generation                   |
|   14. | Integration of distributed renewable energy systems (RES) into the smart grid |
|   15. | Environmental impacts of renewable energy                                     |

## Self-study Lab or Workshop

Every lecture has an assignment. The submission deadline will be given at the end  of  the  lecture.  All  works  presented  must  meet  professional  standards regarding  materials  and  format. The  homework  occupies  20%  of  the  total grade of the course.

Since  it  is  a  faculty's  strong  belief  that  a  student's  success  is  directly proportional to success with homework, it is imperative that the homework should be done. It is the expressed policy of the faculty of the department to take decisive action involving any incidence relating to academic dishonesty. The  instructor  of this course  will strictly enforce  this policy! No  late homework will be accepted .

At least 3 hours per week

Yes

Lab 1:   Integration of DC/DC converters with MPPT (Maximum Power Point Tracking) to a PV generating system; operation and control;

Lab 2:   Integration of DC/AC inverters with MPPT to a PV generating system; operation and control;

Lab 3:  Simulate operation and control of WT generating systems such as DFIG-based wind generation system, PMSG-based wind generation system, and SCIGbased wind generation system;

Module title

Digital Signals &amp; Systems

Module code

61ECE312

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer

| Type               | Lecturer        | Lecturer   | Email              | Office    | Office hours (if any)   | Office hours (if any)   |
|--------------------|-----------------|------------|--------------------|-----------|-------------------------|-------------------------|
| Module Coordinator | Dr. Nguyen Hien | Minh       | hien.nm@vgu.edu.vn | B111      | 10:00-11:00 Fri         | AM,                     |
| Lecturer           | Dr. Nguyen Hien | Minh       | hien.nm@vgu.edu.vn | B111      | 10:00-10:00 Fri         | AM,                     |
| Tutorial           | Dr. Nguyen Hien | Minh       | hien.nm@vgu.edu.vn | B103 B107 | 10:00-11:00 Fri         | AM,                     |

Classification

- [x] ☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

Semester

Winter Semester

Student workload

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency: The module is offered once per academic year

## Prerequisites:

-  Proficiency  in  fundamentals  of  engineering  mathematics:  differential  equations,  difference equations, complex exponentials, probability and statistics.
- Familiar with basic concepts of electric circuits, Laplace transform for circuit analysis.
- Familiar with basic concepts of analog signals and systems.
- Familiar with basic concepts of digital signal processing.

## Applicability for other modules:

Relates to the modules Electric Circuits, Analog Signals &amp; Systems, Digital Signal Processing

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Recognize the terminology that is used in the signal processing field, represent digital signals and basic concepts of digital systems.
2. Obtain deepened knowledge in processing digital signals in information technology and feedback  systems.  Apply  Least-squares  fit  method  to  estimate  parameters  of  digital, linear time-invariant systems.
3. Design digital filters with given hardware constraints.
4. Explain the theory and concepts behind the treatment of random signals in linear digital systems.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
|-------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Overview of Signals and systems Signal representation: continuous-time and discrete-time, digital and analog. Linear shift- time invariant systems. Fourier Series, Fourier transform, Laplace transform, z-transform. Linear shift-time invariant system representation. System transfer function, block diagrams, poles and zeros. Convolution, impulse response and frequency response. Application to circuit analysis. |
|    2. | Overview of signal sampling and reconstruction Nyquist sampling theorem, discrete-time systems. Aliasing. A/D and D/A converters.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
|    3. | Digital systems and processes System analysis and identification of processes. Least-squares fit method and its application to parameter estimation of linear digital systems. ARMA processes.                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
|    4. | Digital filter design FIR and IIR filter, filter order and block diagram realization. Design of FIR filter using windowing method. Design of IIR filter using approximation of derivates and bilinear transformation methods.                                                                                                                                                                                               |
|    5. | Random signals in linear digital systems Random variable. Probability distribution function, probability mass function, cumulative distribution function. Common types of probability distribution functions. Expectation and variance of a random variable. Correlation and covariance of random variables. Random signals, stationary random signals. Random signals in linear digital systems.                           |
|    6. | Review Applications of signals and systems in communications, control and medical imaging technologies.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
