Module title

Electronic Circuits

Module code

61ECE313

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type    | Lecturer           | Email               | Office   | Office hours (if any)      |
|---------|--------------------|---------------------|----------|----------------------------|
| Lecture | Dr. Bui Minh Duong | duong.bm@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon and Fri |
| Lab     | Mr. Vo Van Phung   | phung.vv@vgu.edu.vn | B107     | None                       |

Classification:

☒

Compulsory

☐

Compulsory optional

Semester:

Winter Semester

## Student workload:

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered for each academic year

Prerequisites: 61ECE116 Electric Circuits

Applicability for other modules: 61ECE311 Renewable Energy Systems 1 ; 61ECE321 Renewable  Energy  Systems  2 ; 61ECE323  Electric  Motors  and  Drives ; 61ECE316  Industrial Automation ; and 61ECE308 Smart Grids

## Duration: 15 weeks

## Course description:

This  course  is  to  present  principles  of  power  electronics  and  its  applications.  The  course provides an overview of power semiconductor devices such as Diodes, Thyristors, BJT, MOSFET, and IGBT. The students will also learn analysis and design techniques for switch-mode DC-DC converters (e.g., design, analysis and control of Step-down (Buck), Step-Up (Boost), Buck-Boost and full bridge topologies, pulse-width modulation (PWM)  scheme, characteristics of controllable  switches,  continuous  and  discontinuous  current  mode);  controlled/uncontrolled AC/DC  rectifiers  (e.g.,  single-phase  and  three-phase  diode  rectifiers  with  different  types  of loads,  average  power  output,  performance  parameters,  and  harmonic  analysis);  and  switchmode  DC-AC  converters  (e.g.,  basic  inverter  concept,  and  sinusoidal  PWM).  Moreover,  this course  introduces  operation  of  switching  DC  power  supplies,  and  power  conditioners  and uninterruptible  power  supplies.  The  course  will  emphasize  complex  theoretical  analysis  and computer simulation tools as the course project.

## Intended learning outcomes:

On completion of the course, the students can be able to:

-  Explain static and dynamic characteristics of fundamental power semiconductor devices;
-  Explain  the  working  principle  of  uncontrolled  rectifiers  and  calculate  the  performance parameters from the average, RMS and peak values of the related circuit parameters;
-  Calculate harmonics in the output and input currents for rectifier operations;
-  Design and analyse various types of switched-mode DC-DC converters;
-  Explain the control of power converters using pulse-width modulation (PWM);
-  Describe the basic working principle of switch-mode DC/AC inverters;

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

1.

3.

-  Simulate simple power  electronic circuits using simulation packages  like Spice or MATLAB/Simulink;
-  Select and design power electronic circuits for applications of renewable energy systems; DC power supplies; and power conditioners and uninterruptible power supplies;

## Contents :

| No.       | Topics                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
|-----------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|           | to Power Electronic Systems 1. Applications of Power Electronics 2. Types of Power Electronic Circuits                                                                                                                                    |
| 2. Diodes | and Rectifiers: Power Diodes and Switched RLC Circuits                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| Diodes    | and Rectifiers: Diode Rectifiers 1. Single-Phase Full-Wave Rectifiers 2. Three-Phase Bridge Rectifiers                                                                                                                                    |
| 4.        | Power Transistors and DC-DC Converters: Power Transistors                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| 5.        | Power Transistors and DC-DC Converters: DC-DC Converters 1. Principle of Step-Down Operation 2. Principle of Step-Up Operation 3. Switching-Mode Regulators: Buck Regulators; Boost Regulators; Buck-Boost Regulators; and Cúk Regulators |
| 6.        | Power DC/AC Inverters 1. Single-Phase Bridge Inverters 2. Three-Phase Inverters                                                                                                                                                           |
| 7.        | Thyristors and Thyristorized Converters: Thyristors                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| 8.        | Thyristors and Thyristorized Converters: Controlled Rectifiers 1. Single-Phase Full Converters 2. Three-Phase Full Converters                                                                                                             |
| 9.        | AC Voltage Controllers 1. Single-Phase Full-Wave Controllers 2. Three-Phase Full-Wave Controllers                                                                                                                                         |
| 10.       | Switching DC Power Supplies                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| 11.       | Power Conditioners and Uninterruptible Power Supplies                                                                                                                                                                                     |

Module title

Mobile Communications

Module code

61ECE314

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer

| Type               | Lecturer                 | Email               | Office   | Office hours (if any)   |
|--------------------|--------------------------|---------------------|----------|-------------------------|
| Module Coordinator | Dr. Thai Truyen Dai Chan | chan.ttd@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | 9am-11am, Mon- Fri      |
| Lecturer           | Dr. Thai Truyen Dai Chan | chan.ttd@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | 9am-11am, Mon- Fri      |
| Lab                | Msc. Tran Quang Nhu      | nhu.tq@vgu.edu.vn   | B.101    | 9am-11am, Mon- Fri      |

Classification

☒ Compulsory

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

Semester

Winter Semester

## Student workload

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency

The module is offered each academic year.

Prerequisites

None

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Understand the cause
2. Understand the causes of fading, classify fading and know methods to cope with it;
3. Calculate the multiuser capacity for a specific network scenario;
4. Understand opportunistic communications;
5. Understand  the  spatial multiplexing, channel modeling  and  diversity-multiplexing tradeoff of MIMO;
6. Calculate the capacity of a MIMO system;
7. Know basic concepts of cellular networks and next-generation networks;
8. Know the principles and methods to do network planning;
9. Understand  risks  and  challenges  of  security  of  a  wireless  network,  and  know  basic techniques to sovle.

## Contents

| No.   | Topic                                                 |
|-------|-------------------------------------------------------|
|       | 1.Fading Channels I: Characterization and Signaling   |
| 2.    | Fading Channels II: Capacity and Coding               |
| 3.    | Multiuser Capacity and Opportunistic Communication    |
| 4.    | MIMO I: Spatial Multiplexing and Channel Modeling     |
| 5.    | MIMO II: Capacity and Diversity-Multiplexing Tradeoff |
| 6.    | Cellular Networks                                     |
| 7.    | Network Planning                                      |
| 8.    | Wireless Security                                     |
| 9.    | Next Generation Networks                              |

| Lab          | The course includes 3 lab exercises on abc as follows                                                                                |

## Prerequisites

1. Understanding basic principles of Computer Networks;

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Understand  what  are  the  common  threats  faced  today,  what  are  the  foundational theory behind information security, what are the basic principles and techniques when designing a secure system;
2. Think adversarially, how today's attacks and defenses work in practice;
3. Assess threats for their significance;
4. Gauge the protections and limitations provided by today's technology.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                      |
|-------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Basic Concepts in Cryptography Block and stream ciphers; cryptographic hash functions, public and private key encryption; message authentication; digital signatures; and password system. |
|    2. | System Security Secure design principles; TCB and security kernel construction; system defense against memory exploits; UNIX security; and Windows security.                               |
|    3. | Network Security TCP/IP security issues; DNS security issues and defenses, TLS/SSL; and the AH and ESP protocols.                                                                          |
|    4. | Operational Security Network intrusion detection and prevention systems; and firewalls;                                                                                                    |
|    5. | Securing Wireless LANs                                                                                                                                                                     |

|    | Wired Equivalent Privacy.                                                                                                                                           |
|----|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 6. | Software Security Vulnerability auditing, penetration testing; sandboxing; and control flow integrity.                                                              |
| 7. | Web Security User authentication, authentication-via-secret and session management; and cross site scripting, cross site request forgery, SQL injection.            |
| 8. | Legal and Ethical Issues Cybercrime and computer crime; intellectual property, copyright, patent, trade secret; hacking and intrusion; and privacy, identity theft. |

Prerequisites

## 61ECE304 Industrial sensors &amp; Actuators and 61ECE210 Control Engineering

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Understand and Explain the fundamentals of automation technology and application for manufacturing technology;
2. Describe  the  basic  functions/levels  of  elements  in  an  automated  system;  select appropriate  sensors,  actuators  and  how  to operate  motors  and  motor  controls  for automation;
3. Know-how to model and design a manufacturing automation system with PLC.
4. Employ control methods and procedures;
5. Know how to design intelligent manufacturing systems using the IoT technology
6. Understanding the applications and advances of industrial robots in manufacturing
7. Incorporate proper set-up, maintenance, and testing for automation.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
|-------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Introduction to industrial automation Terminologies and some concepts; Current trends in automation in manufacturing ; Major roles of automation in manufacturing; Automation applications in manufacturing; Components of an automated systems in manufacturing; Hardware components for automation systems; Levels of Industrial Automations. |

The module is offered each academic year

|   2. | Sensor, Actuator, Communication, Interface, and Applications Sensor Technology; Actuator Technology; Communication Technology; Interface Devices Technology; Other Devices for industrial automation.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
|------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|   3. | Control Technology Industrial Control Systems; PLC (concepts, hardware, components, constructions…); PLC- Programming of Ladder Logic (LAD): (Bit Logic Instructions, Comparison Instructions, Conversion Instructions, Counter Instructions, Timer Instructions, Data Block Instructions, Logic Control Instructions, Integer Math Instructions, Floating Point Math Instructions, Move Instructions, Program Control Instructions, Programming Examples) |
|   4. | Case Studies: Automation Systems in Manufacturing CNC machines; Image-based automation; Robot Integrated Shoe Manufacturing; Robot Control in Material Handle in Manufacturing; Smart Factory                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
|   5. | Support systems for Industrial Automation Industrial Robots; Material Transport Systems; Process Monitoring; Conveyor Systems; Cranes and Hoists; Automated Storage/Retrieval Systems; Automated Identification and Data Capture (AIDC)                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
|   6. | Manufacturing Automation and Industry 4.0 Introduction to Automated Assembly Systems, Automated Production Lines and Fundamentals of Industry 4.0                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |

The students will have a comprehensive knowledge of hardware design and programming of the most important features in C; the topics include the recording and processing of analog and digital data, response to interrupt and scheduled events, data transfer via interfaces, data display on LC displays, control of the actuators.

3. They will be familiar with a range of intelligent and adaptive algorithms and demonstrate practical skills in implementing a range of embedded systems like intelligent barcode readers and adaptive color sensors.

-  Camera network configuration and create image acquisition node
-  Image filtering: 2D convolution, averaging, gaussian blurring, median blurring, Sobel Operator and Canny Operator.
-  Binarization and finding the center of mass of the object.
-  Lab Report and code submitted
-  Lab Experiment 4: SLAM (Simultaneous Localization and Mapping)
-  Installation package simulation robot
-  Robot  Mapping  using  Adapted  Monte  Carlo  Localization  (AMCL) Algorithms.
-  Simulation the virtual Turtlebot3 and  connecting with the real Turtlebot3.

Online interaction: The e-learning platform will count the frequency of logging into the site and giving comments. Students' comments will be viewed to access the quality of comments. (10 marks)

Mini tests: 3 mini tests. Each test gets 10 marks. The grade of this part will be the average of the marks of the 2 mini tests. Short answers. In class test

Assignments: 5 assignments. Submission of each assignment gets 2 marks.

Group project (10 marks) Criteria to get maximum grade or excellent group project report. Penalties for late submission of group project report:

- If the report is submitted up to one calendar week after the original deadline (or any formally agreed extension to the deadline): 10% of the total marks available for the piece of work will be deducted from the mark for each working day (or part thereof) following the deadline up to a total of five working days.
-  If  the  report  is  submitted  more  than  five  working  days  after  the  original  deadline  (or  any formally agreed extension to the deadline): a mark of zero will be recorded.

- Length of examination: 90 minutes

- No materials, reference is allowed in the exam room.

## Frequency Prerequisites

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites for module participation: None

Prerequisites for module examination: Laboratory test

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Students  know the  architectural  features  of  the  main  industrial  used  field  buses.  You know the essential requirements for fieldbus systems as well as the characteristics of the most important fieldbuses used in the industrial environment.
2. Students  are  able  to  fieldbus  according  to  the  project  requirements  to  select  and  to project.
3. The students expand their competences in the field of teamwork and and Presentation techniques

## Contents

| No.   | Topic                                                                                 |
|-------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|       | 1.Introduction to industrial communication networks                                   |
| 2.    | Transmission methods, IOS module, physical media, and network topology                |
| 3.    | Transmission methods, IOS module, physical media, and network topology                |
| 4.    | Interconnection products: Repeater, Hub, Switch, Transceiver, Bridge, Router, Gateway |
| 5.    | ASi, Ethernet - TCP/IP - Modbus, Profinet, Profibus - DP, DNP3, and IEC61850          |

|   6. | SCADA functions and applications   |

Module title

Renewable Energy Systems 2

Module code

61ECE321

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type    | Lecturer           | Email               | Office   | Office hours (if any)      |
|---------|--------------------|---------------------|----------|----------------------------|
| Lecture | Dr. Bui Minh Duong | duong.bm@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon and Fri |
| Lab     | Mr. Vo Van Phung   | phung.vv@vgu.edu.vn | B107     | None                       |

Classification:

☒ Compulsory

Semester:

Summer Semester

Student workload:

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites: 61ECE116 Electric Circuits

Applicability for other modules:

61ECE308 Smart Grids

Duration:

15 weeks

## Course description:

This  course  provides  a  systematic  introduction  to  basic  concepts  and  key  technologies  of microgrids.  The  course  also  introduces  modelling,  operation  and  control,  steady-state  and dynamic analysis of microgrids with energy storage systems (ESS). The course discusses major electricity storage technologies in depth along with their efficiency, lifetime cycles, environmental  benefits  and  capacity,  so  that  the  students  can  select  which  type  of  storage technology  is  best  for  a  particular  microgrid  application.  Moreover,  different  solutions  are mentioned to find the proper sizing of ESS for the microgrid as well as to design ESS control systems for integrating with the microgrid. The students are taught to analyze power flows and calculate  fault  currents  and  voltages  in  order  to  design  a  basic  protection  system  of  the microgrid.

## Intended learning outcomes:

On the successful completion of this module, the learners can be able to:

-  Select different energy storage technologies to be appropriate for particular microgrid applications;
-  Design,  operate  and  control  power-electronic  converters/technologies  to  efficiently interface between energy storage systems (ESS) and microgrids;
-  Regulate  voltage,  frequency  and  power  in  the  microgrid  through  using  the  ESS integrated with renewable-energy distributed generators;
-  Find the proper sizing of ESS for the microgrid as well as design the ESS control systems for integrating with the microgrid;

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

-  Analyze power flows and calculate fault currents and voltages in order to design a basic protection system of the microgrid;
-  Get presentation and teamwork skills and time-management skills for the on-time submission of assignments;

## Contents :

|   No. | Topics                                                                          |
|-------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Basic Concepts and Control Architecture of Microgrids                           |
|    2. | Energy Storage Technologies                                                     |
|    3. | Applications of Energy Storage System (ESS) in Renewable Energy Microgrids      |
|    4. | Interfacing Between an ESS and a Microgrid through Power-Electronic Circuits    |
|    5. | Coordinated Frequency Regulation of BESS with Renewable Generation in Microgrid |
|    6. | Proper Sizing of Energy Storage Systems for Microgrids                          |
|    7. | LOAD FLOW ANALYSIS OF POWER GRIDS AND MICROGRIDS                                |
|    8. | POWER GRID AND MICROGRID FAULT STUDIES                                          |
|    9. | Protection of the microgrid                                                     |

Module title

High-Voltage Engineering

Module code

61ECE322

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type    | Lecturer           | Email               | Office   | Office hours (if any)      |
|---------|--------------------|---------------------|----------|----------------------------|
| Lecture | Dr. Bui Minh Duong | duong.bm@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon and Fri |
| Lab     | Mr. Vo Van Phung   | phung.vv@vgu.edu.vn | B107     |                            |

Classification:

☒ Compulsory

Semester:

Summer Semester

Student workload:

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites: 61ECE116 Electric Circuits; and 61ECE204 Electromagnetics

Applicability for other modules:

61ECE308 Smart Grids

Duration:

15 weeks

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

## Course description:

This course is to provide students with an introduction to high voltage engineering, phenomena and technology. The course helps students to understand high voltage generation, measurement and testing, transient overvoltages, and the protection of high voltage apparatus. Generally, the content of the course consists of: generation of high voltages, measurement of high  voltages,  electrostatic  fields  and  field  stress  control,  electrical  breakdown  in  gases, breakdown  in  solid  and  liquid  dielectrics,  non-destructive  insulation  test  techniques,  overvoltages,  testing  procedures  and  insulation  coordination,  and  design  and  testing  of  external insulation.

## Intended learning outcomes:

Upon completion of this course, the students can be able to:

-  Understand and apply principles of  theory of high voltage generation and measurements;
-  Analyze transient overvoltages and design protection;
-  Describe and explain the operation of high voltage power supplies for ac, dc, and impulse voltages;
-  Get familiar with various applications where high voltage field is used;
-  Understand breakdown of high-voltage (HV) insulation (solid, liquid and gas);
-  Understand lightning phenomena and HV insulation environmental pollution;
-  Know the methods of analytical and numerical calculation of electric fields;
-  Calculate the electric field and analyze them with COMSOL Multiphysics;
-  Calculate, construct and evaluate a high voltage construction with respect to electric fields as well as materials with respect to insulation;

## Contents :

| No.       | Topics                                                                                                                               |
|-----------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 1.        | Introduction to High-Voltage Engineering                                                                                             |
| 2.        | Generation of high voltages                                                                                                          |
| 3.        | Measurement of high voltages                                                                                                         |
| 4.        | Electrostatic fields and field stress control                                                                                        |
| 5.        | Electrical breakdown in gases                                                                                                        |
| 6.        | Breakdown in solid and liquid dielectrics (Electrical breakdown in HV insulation (Solid, Liquid and Gas) and HV insulation Pollution |
| 7.        | Non-destructive insulation test techniques                                                                                           |
| 8.        | Over-voltages, testing procedures and insulation coordination                                                                        |
| 9. Design | and testing of external insulation                                                                                                   |

Module title

Electric Motors and Drives

Module code

61ECE323

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type    | Lecturer                               | Email               | Office   | Office hours (if any)      |
|---------|----------------------------------------|---------------------|----------|----------------------------|
| Lecture | Dr. Bui Minh Duong duong.bm@vgu.edu.vn | B111                |          | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon and Fri |
| Lab     | Mr. Vo Van Phung                       | phung.vv@vgu.edu.vn | B107     | None                       |

Classification:

☒

Compulsory

Semester:

☐

Summer

Compulsory optional

Semester

Student workload:

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered each academic year

Prerequisites: 61ECE116 Electric Circuits and 61ECE204 Electromagnetics

Duration:

15 weeks

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

## Course description:

The aim of this course is to equip students with basic knowledge of variable-speed drives and motion  control  systems  which  are  used  in  many  industrial  processes  such  as  in  conveyors, machine  tools,  pumps,  compressors,  mining  drives,  electric  vehicles,  ship  propulsion,  wind energy systems, air-craft actuators, servo drives and automation systems,… The course stresses the  basic  understanding  of  the  characteristics  of  machines  driven  by  appropriate  power electronic  converters  and  controllers.  The  steady-state  behaviour  of  such  drives  will  be primarily covered and some dynamic issues of drive representation and control system design will also be introduced.

More detailed, this course introduces five main contents as the following:

- i. Electrical Drive Systems : fundamentals (translational and rotational motion, power rating and classes of duty, 4-quadrant operation, torque/power limits, note on closed-loop control of drives, and electrical and mechanical transformers);
- ii. DC drives : brushed and brushless DC motors (conventional DC motors, modern DC motors), and introduction to their control issues…;
- iii. AC motor drives : examples of motor drives (e.g. induction motors, synchronous motors), and introduction to their control issues (emphasize model based control characteristics, nonlinearity involved);
- iv. Servo motors and stepper motors : principles and their control;
- v. Examples of modern electrical drives in engineering applications;

## Intended learning outcomes:

Upon completion of this module, the students can be able to:

1. Understand fundamental elements of drive systems; and analyze the steady-state characteristics of a few commonly used types of drives used in the industry;
2. Understand the performance of these drives supplied from appropriate converters;
3. Understand the quadrant operation of various types of drives and their control requirements, selection of converters, and components;
4. Design hierarchical control structures for drive systems of different machines;
5. Select and design important elements of a drive system;
6. Apply theories of electrical machines, power electronic converters and control engineering to implement drive systems of electric motors which are appropriate for specific performances;

## Contents :

|   No. | Topics                                                                     |
|-------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Chapter One - Electric Motors - The Basics                                 |
|    2. | Chapter Two - Introduction to Power Electronic Converters for Motor Drives |
|    3. | Chapter Three - Conventional D.C. Motors                                   |

|   4. | Chapter Four - D.C. Motor Drives                                             |
|------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|   5. | Chapter Five - DC MACHINES AND DRIVES                                        |
|   6. | Chapter Six - Induction Motors - Rotating Field, Slip and Torque             |
|   7. | Chapter Seven - Induction Motors - Operation from 50/60Hz Supply             |
|   8. | Chapter Eight - Variable Frequency Operation of Induction Motors             |
|   9. | Chapter Nine - Inverter-fed Induction Motor Drives                           |
|  10. | Chapter Ten - Synchronous and Brushless Permanent Magnet Machines and Drives |
|  11. | Chapter Eleven - Stepping and Switched-reluctance Motors                     |
|  12. | Chapter Twelve - Motor/Drive Selection                                       |

Module title

Power Electronics

Module code

62ECE324

Study program

Electrical and Computer Engineering (ECE)

## Module coordinator/Lecturer:

| Type    | Lecturer           | Email               | Office   | Office hours (if any)      |
|---------|--------------------|---------------------|----------|----------------------------|
| Lecture | Dr. Bui Minh Duong | duong.bm@vgu.edu.vn | B111     | 9:00-11:00 AM, Mon and Fri |
| Lab     | Mr. Vo Van Phung   | phung.vv@vgu.edu.vn | B107     | None                       |

Classification:

☒ Compulsory

Semester:

Summer Semester

- [ ] ☐ Compulsory optional

- [ ] ☐ Optional/Elective

## Student workload:

| Credits                              |   5 | ECTS   |
|--------------------------------------|-----|--------|
| Contact hours                        |  60 | AHs    |
| Assignments and independent learning |  90 | AHs    |
| Total Working hours                  | 150 | AHs    |

Frequency:

The module is offered for each academic year

Prerequisites: 61ECE116 Electric Circuits

Applicability for other modules: 61ECE311 Renewable Energy Systems 1 ; 61ECE321 Renewable  Energy  Systems  2 ; 61ECE323  Electric  Motors  and  Drives ; 61ECE316  Industrial Automation ; and 61ECE308 Smart Grids

Duration:

15 weeks

## Course description:

This  course  is  to  present  principles  of  power  electronics  and  its  applications.  The  course provides an overview of power semiconductor devices such as Diodes, Thyristors, BJT, MOSFET, and IGBT. The students will also learn analysis and design techniques for switch-mode DC-DC converters (e.g., design, analysis and control of Step-down (Buck), Step-Up (Boost), Buck-Boost and full bridge topologies, pulse-width modulation (PWM)  scheme, characteristics of controllable  switches,  continuous  and  discontinuous  current  mode);  controlled/uncontrolled AC/DC  rectifiers  (e.g.,  single-phase  and  three-phase  diode  rectifiers  with  different  types  of loads,  average  power  output,  performance  parameters,  and  harmonic  analysis);  and  switchmode  DC-AC  converters  (e.g.,  basic  inverter  concept,  and  sinusoidal  PWM).  Moreover,  this course introduces application of power electronic circuits for renewable energy systems, the operation of switching DC power supplies, and power conditioners and uninterruptible power supplies. The course will emphasize complex theoretical analysis and computer simulation tools as the course project.

## Intended learning outcomes:

On completion of the course, the students can be able to:

-  Explain static and dynamic characteristics of fundamental power semiconductor devices;
-  Explain  the  working  principle  of  uncontrolled  rectifiers  and  calculate  the  performance parameters from the average, RMS and peak values of the related circuit parameters;
-  Calculate harmonics in the output and input currents for rectifier operations;
-  Design and analyse various types of switched-mode DC-DC converters;
-  Explain the control of power converters using pulse-width modulation (PWM);
-  Describe the basic working principle of switch-mode DC/AC inverters;
-  Simulate simple power  electronic circuits using simulation packages  like Spice or MATLAB/Simulink;
-  Select and design power electronic circuits for applications of renewable energy systems; DC power supplies; and power conditioners and uninterruptible power supplies;

## Contents :

|   No. | Topics                                                                        |
|-------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|     1 | Introduction to Power Electronic Systems 1. Applications of Power Electronics |

|       | 2. Types of Power Electronic Circuits                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
|-------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 2     | Power Diodes and Rectifiers: Power Diodes and Switched RLC Circuits                                                                                                                                                                       |
| 3     | Power Diodes and Rectifiers: Diode Rectifiers 1. Single-Phase Full-Wave Rectifiers 2. Three-Phase Bridge Rectifiers                                                                                                                       |
| 4     | Power Transistors and DC-DC Converters: Power Transistors                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| 5     | Power Transistors and DC-DC Converters: DC-DC Converters 1. Principle of Step-Down Operation 2. Principle of Step-Up Operation 3. Switching-Mode Regulators: Buck Regulators; Boost Regulators; Buck-Boost Regulators; and Cúk Regulators |
| 6     | Power DC/AC Inverters 1. Single-Phase Bridge Inverters 2. Three-Phase Inverters                                                                                                                                                           |
| 7     | Thyristors and Thyristorized Converters: Thyristors                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| 8     | Thyristors and Thyristorized Converters: Controlled Rectifiers 1. Single-Phase Full Converters 2. Three-Phase Full Converters                                                                                                             |
| 9. AC | Voltage Controllers 1. Single-Phase Full-Wave Controllers 2. Three-Phase Full-Wave Controllers                                                                                                                                            |
| 10.   | Application of Power Electronics for Renewable Energy                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| 11.   | Switching DC Power Supplies                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| 12.   | Power Conditioners and Uninterruptible Power Supplies                                                                                                                                                                                     |

## Integrity:

Academic dishonesty is a completely unacceptable mode of conduct and will not be tolerated in any form. All  persons involved in academic dishonesty will be disciplined in accordance with University regulations and procedures. Discipline may include suspension or expulsion from the University. 'Scholastic dishonesty includes but is not limited to cheating, plagiarism, collusion, and the submission for credit of any work or materials that are attributable in whole or in part to another person, taking an examination for another person, any act designed to give unfair advantage to a student or the attempt to commit such acts.'

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Be fundamentally familiar with modern operating systems and virtualization techniques;
2. Know  the  most  important  concepts  and  mechanisms  of  operating  systems  and virtualization techniques;
3. Select and use appropriate operating systems for appropriate use cases;
4. Implement and use system-level software;
5. Analyze and extend the behavior of operating systems;
6. Select and deploy suitable virtualization solutions for corresponding applications.

## Frequency Prerequisites

Once each academic year

Knowledge of Vector Calculus is an advantage. Learners will be expected to be familiar with DC and AC circuit analysis.

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Demonstrate  capacity  to  explain  qualitatively  and  quantitatively  the  concepts  of electromagnetic  waves  in  different  transmission  media,  polarized  plane  waves  and plane wave reflection in mathematical form.
2. Demonstrate  capacity  to  carry  out  the  design  of  microwave  circuits  using  advanced simulation tools, including electromagnetic simulations.
3. Select suitable measurement methodologies to characterize and verify the performance of  microwave  circuits  and  devices  and  undertake  measurements  to  characterize  and verify the performance of microwave circuits and devices.
4. Explain /compare the various circuit fabrication technologies and select the appropriate technology for a particular application and justify that selection.
5. Communicate findings through written reports.
6. Carry out a substantial research-based project.

## Contents

|   No. | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
|-------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|    1. | Lecture 1: Introduction  Circuit technology options for wireless RF/Microwave circuit implementation  Semiconductor devices  Fundamental Concepts  Maxwell's Equations, slow waves, fast waves, Hansen Woodyard criteria                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
|    2. | Fundamentals of transmission line theory  Analysis  Discussion on the propagation constant and characteristic wave impedance  Lossless line  Lossy transmission line  The reflection coefficient in the frequency domain  The smith chart  Impedance matching  Quarter-wave impedance transformer  Tapered impedance transformer  Directional coupler  Power splitter  Group velocity  Slow waves or fast waves |

4.

5.

8.

## Scattering parameters

-  Definition of wave amplitudes
-  Definition of S-parameters
3. 
- 2-port
-  Useful definitions
-  Lossless networks
-  Use of n-port S-parameters for nonlinear analysis
-  Network analyzer

## RF Front-end Designs

-  High frequency performance of lumped passive components.
-  Microwave transmission lines - design and analysis.
-  Microwave couplers and filters.
-  Active microwave devices.
-  Low noise amplifier design (Stability Analysis)
-  Power amplifier design.
-  Oscillator and mixer design.

## Practical Transmission lines

-  Guided and unguided structure
-  Polarization
-  Transverse electric modes, rectangular wave guides
-  Transverse electromagnetic modes, microstrip line, coplanar waveguides, slot lines
-  Transverse magnetic modes, Goubau line, single-wire transmission line, surface waves.
-  Implementation of passive components using different guiding structures.

## Microwave amplifier

-  Y-parameters
-  2-port described by y-parameters
-  Stability of a 2-port
-  Stability factor
6.  Stabilization of an active device
-  Power gain definitions
-  Unilateral transistor
-  Bilateral transistor
-  Optimum input and output matching
-  Maximum available power gain
-  Different amplifier concepts

## 7. Microwave circuit measurement and characterization techniques.

## RF Front-end and Antenna

-  Transmitter receiver system
-  Transmitter-receiver-system as quadrupole
-  General concept of antennas:  antenna Gain, impedance, directivity, beam-width, radiation patterns, far field, dipole and monopole.
-  High Q filter
-  Low noise amplifier
-  Monopole antennas
-  Patch antennas
-  Spoofed Surface Plasmon Polariton
-  Leaky wave antennas
-  Endfire antennas
-  Mixers, Uplink and downlink

Module title

Digital Routing

Prerequisites None

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Understand principles of routing in different network architectures.
2. Know how shortest- and widest-path routing algorithms and different protocols work.
3. Know different routing protocols in IP networks, such as but not limited to OSPF and BGP, and engineer traffic.
4. Understand routing in public switching telephone networks and its SS7 signalling system.

| 5.    | IP routing and distance vector protocol family    |
| 6.    | OSPF and integrated IS-IS                         |

|   7. | IP traffic engineering                                         |

|   8. | BGP                                                            |
|   9. | Hierarchical and dynamic call routing in the telephone network |

| Group work   | Each group work on a project and present in the class.                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| Self-study   | Students read materials and work on exercises at home.                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| Lab          | The course includes 2 lab sessions as follows  Session 1: Analyzing IP packets by using network protocol analyzer Wireshark.  Session 2: Building, configuring, troubleshooting IP network topology related to VLAN, static routing, dynamic routing protocols. |

## Mode of Assessment

## Group project with Presentation (10%)

-  All topics of the projects are registered by students at the beginning of the module and the tentative date of the presentation of each group determined.

## Lab

-  A student needs to register, participate in, and pass the lab in order to be eligible for participating in the final exam.

## Exams (90%)

-  Length of examination: 90 minutes.
-  Printed and written materials are allowed.
-  All electronic devices are NOT allowed except individual calculator.

## Grading policy

| Assessment method         |   Percentage of total | Assessment date                  |
|---------------------------|-----------------------|----------------------------------|
| Project with Presentation |                    10 | Specified for each student group |
| Final exam/Written exam   |                    90 | Notified before the module       |
| Total                     |                   100 |                                  |

## Module materials

## Required texts

1. 'Network  Routing  Algorithms,  Protocols,  and  Architectures,'  1st  Edition,  Deepankar Medhi and Karthikeyan Ramasamy.

## Student workload

Frequency

Once each academic year

## Prerequisites

## No prerequisite is needed.

## Intended learning outcomes

On successful completion of this module the learner will be able to:

1. Carry out a substantial research-based project
2. Demonstrate capacity to author a journal-grade paper in IEEE-compliant Latex format.
3. Demonstrate capacity to lead and manage change through collaboration with others
4. Demonstrate an understanding of the ethical issues associated with research
5. Analyze data and synthesize research findings
6. Report research findings in written and verbal forms
7. Use  research  findings  to  advance  theory  and  practice  in  the  field  of  the  learners' choices.

## Contents

| No.   | Topic                             |
|-------|-----------------------------------|
|       | 1.Basic Concepts                  |
| o     | The meaning of publish or perish. |

## Learning activities

| Activities             | Explanation                                                                                                                              |
|------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Attendance             | Students should attend 100%. Attendance will be checked every lesson. There is no grade for the attendance completion.                   |
| Individual Assignments | Regular classroom assignments will be given to enhance the students' learning and development.                                           |
| Group work             | Each 5-member group will be guided to write and submit a journal-grade paper. They will be guided to respond to the reviewers' comments. |
| Online Activities      | A forum will be created on VGU's e-learning platform for student discussion and share on topics, group and individual works.             |

## Mode of Assessment

Online interaction: The e-learning platform will count the frequency of logging into the site and giving comments.  Students'  comments  will  be  viewed  to  access the quality of comments. (5 marks)

Assignments: Classroom assignments will be given right after each lesson. (10 marks)

Group project Criteria to get maximum grade or excellent group project report.

Students will be divided into groups. Each group will be guided by the instructor to co-author a journal-grade paper. Each group will be guided to submit their work to an open-access journal for consideration of publication. Their work will be graded according to the following criteria:

- 1) If a group receives 'an acceptance with minor revision' from the reviewers, their grade will be highest (80 marks).
- 2) If a group receives 'a reject with major revision' from the reviewers, their grade will be 50 marks.
- 4) If a group receives 'a reject and resubmission discouraged' from the reviewers, their grade will be 30 marks.
- 4) If a group's work is rejected by managing editors without being passed to the reviewers, the group will either accept 10 marks or resubmit their paper.

## Exams

- Oral presentation: 15 minutes

- No materials, reference is allowed in the exam room.

## Grading policy

| Assessment method   | Percentage of total   | Assessment date          |
|---------------------|-----------------------|--------------------------|
| Online interaction  | 5                     | Frequently               |
| Oral examination    | 5                     | At the end of the course |
|                     | Frequently            | Class Assignments 10     |
| Group project 80    |                       | At the end of the course |
| Total               | 100                   |                          |

2. R. W. Murray, 'Skillful Writing of an Awful Research Paper', Anal. Chem, 83, 633, 2011
